Hitler's Declaration: Willing to Join Hands with All Countries; Never Allow Communism to Rise Again, and Cites the Spanish Incident as a Warning

Nuremberg: Chancellor Hitler today addressed more than 100,000 stormtroopers and blackshirts, making a solemn statement regarding Germany's desire for peace, saying, "We only have one wish, which is to maintain peace. We already know what war is, so we are very willing to join hands with the people of all countries around us and work together. We have no hostility towards them, but one thing must be made clear, that Germany will never be inclined to Bolshevism. We will never allow the results of our work and the careers created by the hard work of millions of people to be destroyed by some international and Bolshevik Jews. Now, in other countries, the public is often instigated to convene anti-fascist and national socialist rallies, and to support Bolsheviks, and advocate providing them with weapons, money, manpower, etc. I have never convened any similar rallies in my life, but if there is an opportunity to convene one, the number of participants will definitely be more than 10,000 to 30,000, but will have millions of people. In addition, there will be millions more people who raise their hands in favor of resisting our old enemies, the parasites of humanitarianism."

Hitler then had an informal conversation with Reuters reporters during lunch, first explaining the reasons why this year's National Socialist Party Congress focused on attacking Bolshevism. The lunch was held in a 700-year-old castle, which was ideally located with a view over the ancient city of Nuremberg. Those present at the lunch included Hitler's confidant Hess, the newly appointed German Ambassador to the UK Ribbentrop, and many foreign reporters. Hitler was still wearing the ordinary brown clothes he had worn during the morning parade, and was in good spirits. When shaking hands with people, he was heavy and enthusiastic. When discussing his speech to the stormtroopers, Hitler also mentioned the anti-fascist demonstrations that had occurred in various countries, saying that at present, other countries are tolerating demonstrations advocating aid to the Spanish Bolsheviks, and openly raising money and weapons for them, but view the Nuremberg Congress as a mobilization of the National Socialist Party. Hitler showed a contemptuous smile when speaking, and also said, "If we followed our usual intentions and instructed the national population to initiate support for the Spanish Nationalist Party, with just one order from me, 10 to 15 million German people would respond. The greatness of this kind of demonstration would be unprecedented in the world, and would definitely make the whole world, even Moscow, feel uncomfortable."

According to Hitler's estimate, the strength of his political force, excluding the army, includes 2 million stormtroopers, 267,000 blackshirts, and 22,000 other teams. Hitler continued, "The world seems to find it strange that we are so strongly opposed to Bolshevism. In fact, it is because we and Italy have experienced the same situation as today's Spain. For example, in Nuremberg in 1923, (Hitler pointed to the chimneys in the distance) 4,500 veterans marched through here and were attacked by communists. Also, in Munich, during the Soviet regime, many pledged people were shot by Bolsheviks, which is no different from today's Spain. Today's Germany is no longer afraid of the invasion of Bolshevism. What is worrying is that the countries around Germany are now being contaminated by this Bolshevik poison, and will each suffer from it. We cannot stand idly by in this situation. It should be known that we are one of the countries in Europe, and we have related relationships with our neighboring countries in terms of culture and commerce. I dare to believe that we 'wild National Socialists' are ultimately the best people in Europe." (13th Reuters Dispatch)

National Socialist Party Congress Closes; Military Parade Held; 400 Airplanes Participate

Nuremberg: Today is the closing day of the 8th annual congress of the National Socialist Party. There were as many as 100,000 people in the audience, all applauding thunderously and shouting "Victory" slogans. Their emotions were excited, as if drunk, especially when airplanes appeared and bombs exploded. The parade is briefly described below. Initially, the various troops practiced, and then they formed a square formation and stood still. Then, a large number of students from the Dobrits Aviation School, holding various flags, entered the field one after another. In addition to the faded Prussian flag of 1813 and the flag of the German Empire, there were also many new military flags of the army, navy, and air force, which were personally awarded by Chancellor Hitler to the newly formed troops. Among them, the infantry flag was black and white, with an iron cross in the center and a small swastika in each of the four corners. The navy flag was blue and white, and the air force flag was red, white, and orange. English, French and Czech Representatives Highly Praise the Red Army's Strength, Especially its Air Force and Tank Corps

(Moscow) The French, Czech, and British military delegations, after observing maneuvers in the Belorussian Military District, have arrived in Moscow and shared their impressions with local journalists as follows:

General Rucha, the Chief Czech Representative, stated, "By deciding to participate in the exercises, the combat effectiveness and training of the various units can be described as exceptionally good. All units have demonstrated extremely strong dynamism. I believe special attention should be paid to the Red Army's infantry and the tactical training of the tank battalions. Your country has adopted new tactics by deploying such a large number of tanks, and the Red Army has been able to solve this complex problem in a short period of time. In this regard, your country is pioneering a new path in military thinking. The commanding officers have demonstrated a high level of tactical and technical training, extreme endurance, noble spirit, and loyalty to the motherland. They are able to quickly solve the most complex problems of modern warfare. The Red Army possesses the latest technology. In my view, it is the most advanced army in the world in this respect. The airborne troops descending from aircraft demonstrated the high level of fighting spirit and courage. Currently, we can say that only the Red Army can deploy troops on a large scale from aircraft. We have seen many meaningful events, which we will try to utilize in our army."

General Chivesgerte and General Flemming, Deputy Chiefs of Staff of the French Army, stated, "We have been greatly impressed by the steadfastness and bravery of the infantry and other units during their movements, as well as the courage of the paratroopers. The tank movements demonstrated the drivers' refined skills. We would like to pay special attention to the extremely good condition of the artillery and the horses used by the cavalry." Mr. Flemming continued, "We admire the orderly formations of the air force and pay particular attention to the fighter planes and high-speed bombers, as well as the skill of their pilots." In conclusion, Mr. Chives spoke of the interest aroused in the French delegation by the nearly completed Minsk Red Army barracks and its sports and cultural facilities.

General Wavell, the leader of the British delegation, stated, "I am familiar with the old Russian army, so I paid special attention to your progress. We admire the soundness of your army and its endurance. The training level of the commanding officers made an excellent impression. We were deeply impressed by the technical development of your infantry, tanks, and aircraft. You have undoubtedly achieved great success in this area. The control of fighter planes during the exercises proved the high level of technical knowledge and skills of the combatants. The paratroopers also demonstrated amazing bravery, fortitude, and good training." Colonel Martel, a well-known British Staff representative and author on tank problems, stated, "I must admit that the tank drivers I saw were excellent. During the entire exercise, only a very small number of tanks were forced to stop on the battlefield due to mechanical or material failures. There were no accidental landings or damage to the aircraft. This fact convinces people of the excellence of your aircraft and tanks and proves the high skill of the tank and air personnel. As for the spectacle of airborne troop deployment, we are seeing it for the first time. The good order during the landings confirms the bravery and high spirit of the paratroopers." (TASS dispatch, 13th)

National Socialist Party Congress: Hitler's Closing Address - Will He Announce a Break in Relations with Russia?

(Berlin) Hitler will deliver an important official speech in Nuremberg tonight. There is much speculation among outsiders about this speech. Some predict that Mr. Hitler will announce the severance of diplomatic relations with Soviet Russia, because cooperation with countries whose principles are fundamentally opposed to National Socialism cannot be beneficial to Germany. (Reuters dispatch, 14th)

(Paris) Le Petit Journal recently reported that as the German National Socialist Party Congress is about to close, the head of state, Hitler, will deliver a final speech tomorrow afternoon, stating that communism will not be tolerated if it interferes with the borders of Germany. "If this statement is interpreted in a milder diplomatic tone, it means that if a communist revolution occurs in France, the new German armed forces will immediately intervene by force," it is said. (Havas dispatch, 13th)

Tense Relations Between Germany and Russia Cause Anxiety Among British Political Figures

(London) The recent tense relations between Germany and Russia have caused considerable anxiety among political figures here. They fear that the impact will jeopardize the future of the Locarno Conference. It is said that the German National Socialist Party Congress's launch of an "anti-Bolshevik crusade" is intended to win the favor of the British people. However, the result is that, apart from the extreme right wing of the Conservative Party, such as Lord Rothermere, and former Colonial Secretary Amery, the other factions have not expressed sympathy. The reason for this is that Germany's movement is too hasty, like a volcanic eruption, and therefore fails to gain people's trust. Officials in Britain are concerned about the international repercussions that may arise. They believe that the most unpredictable aspect of Europe is not Russia, but Germany. Britain should do everything in its power to resolve difficulties and ease the hostile relations between these countries. However, unless the Rhine River problem is resolved simultaneously with general European issues, France will be difficult to satisfy. Even if a new Locarno Pact is concluded, it will be in vain if the dangerous areas of Eastern Europe are ignored. (Havas dispatch, 14th)

(Paris) Regarding the future Locarno Conference, the British government previously notified Italy and Germany of its intention to convene a meeting in late October. According to the Morning Post's correspondent in London, Prince Bismarck, the German Chargé d'Affaires in Britain, visited Sir Westcott, an official of the British Foreign Office, yesterday. He inquired under what conditions the countries involved would resume talks with Germany after the Five-Power Conference, i.e., the Locarno Conference, ended. He stated that if the Soviet Union were allowed to participate in these talks, as rumored, the German government would stay away. Furthermore, thorough diplomatic preparations must be made before the start of the Five-Power Conference, and the plan to hold it in October would be too rushed. (Havas dispatch, 14th)

(London) The Times recently commented on the proceedings of the German National Socialist Party Congress, stating that the German Foreign Ministry did not seem to have any official representatives participating. This raises a question among foreign observers as to how much responsibility the Ministry can still bear for its diplomatic duties. "If the German authorities believe that Britain will assist Germany in eradicating communism so that fascism can dominate Europe, they are misunderstanding the nature of the British people. It is undoubtedly the case that the speeches delivered by the German leaders in Nuremberg were planned in advance, and their intention was to oppose the Franco-Russian alliance treaty (i.e., the mutual assistance pact). However, under the current circumstances, it is impossible to expect the neighboring countries of Germany that have already concluded such treaties to abandon them. In fact, if a general solution to the European problem can be found, so that all alliance treaties concluded by various countries lose their purpose, then it would not only be possible but also desirable. However, this can only be achieved after the causes that led to these alliance treaties have been completely eliminated. In short, both France and Russia are now vigilant and determined to help each other, which is only reasonable," it is said. The Daily Chronicle stated, "Germany is now prepared to bargain over the conclusion of a Western European security agreement. If France is unable to participate in this smaller-scope agreement due to the obligations stipulated in the Franco-Russian mutual assistance pact, then Germany wants to conclude a pact with Britain to counter the Franco-Russian mutual assistance pact." (Havas dispatch, 14th)

Armored Train Attacked - More Than Twenty Japanese Soldiers Killed, More Than Sixty Wounded

(Nanjing) According to the headquarters of the 12th Division in Kyushu today, on Saturday night, about 250 Chinese and Korean bandits attacked a column of armored trains eight kilometers west of Muling County in eastern Manchuria. Japanese soldiers in the train fought a bloody battle with them all night, and finally repelled the bandits. A total of 25 Japanese officers and soldiers were killed and 65 were wounded. Fortunately, all of them flew over their heads and did not injure anyone. (TASS dispatch, 13th)

Sino-British Boxer Indemnity - Students Studying in Britain Arrive in London - Warm Welcome from Concerned Parties

(London) Nineteen Chinese students selected by the British Boxer Indemnity Committee arrived in London today. Miss Li from the University of Hong Kong is also among them. Representatives of Chinese students studying in Britain also welcomed them at the port and distributed welcome letters printed in Chinese to the new students. The letter included a map of the London Underground and bus routes for reference. Several parties in London are preparing to hold a banquet to welcome them, including Mrs. Panli Tuobuluni, wife of the British Consul in Nanjing. As for the banquet of the Chinese Committee of various universities, it has been postponed due to the fact that most of the committee members have not returned to London. All new students will have comfortable residences, and the older students in London will do their best to take care of them. According to Mr. Silcock, who spoke to a Reuters reporter, all the new students are excellent. Among the nineteen new students, except for one who will study aeronautical engineering, the rest will study at universities in England and Scotland. (Reuters dispatch, 14th)

Chilean Ambassador Exerts Efforts to Rescue Women and Children in Endangered Spanish City - Besieged for Seven Weeks Amidst Cannon Fire - Rebels Refuse to Release, Repeated Appeals

The Chilean Ambassador to Madrid, Mr. Moregado, now the leader of the diplomatic corps, set out for Toledo today to do his best to rescue the rebel women and children currently trapped in the historically famous Moorish castle of Alcazar in Spain. Spanish Prime Minister Caballerro has promised to provide all kinds of facilities. If the Alcazar women and children decide to leave the country, all embassies in the capital will provide them with refuge. The garrison of the castle, including women and children, totals one thousand people. They have been besieged for seven weeks and, due to constant cannon fire, one-third of the castle has been reduced to ashes. (Reuters dispatch, 14th)

Madrid The Chilean Ambassador to Madrid, Mr. Mougado, acting leader of the Madrid diplomatic corps, and Mr. Airfang, commercial counselor of the Romanian Legation, visited Spanish Prime Minister Caballerro today to request that they be allowed to rescue the women, children, and elderly people in the Alcazar fortress in Toledo. They proposed to transport these women and children to the capital to take temporary refuge in the embassies of various countries. After a brief conversation, Mr. Mao and Mr. Ai set out by car for Toledo. The Ministry of Military Affairs announced that it learned today that the military commander of Alcazar had consulted on Saturday about surrendering to the government forces. (Guomin dispatch, 13th)

Madrid The leader of the rebel forces trapped in the Alcazar fortress today refused to negotiate with representatives of the diplomatic corps on the issue of releasing residents. The attempt to rescue the six hundred women and children in the fortress has failed. Mr. Mugado, the Chilean Ambassador to Spain, and Mr. Ilfin, the commercial counselor of Romania, personally went to the front line to contact the government authorities on ways to rescue the women and children in the fortress and send them to monasteries near Madrid. Spanish Prime Minister Caballerro also personally went to Toledo to participate in the negotiations and immediately accepted the recommendations of the diplomatic corps. Government soldiers then took a loudspeaker to a point ten yards away from the fortress and loudly announced to the rebel leader that the Chilean Ambassador was willing to talk to them. If they agreed, they were asked to raise a white flag as a sign of truce. After shouting five times, there was no response. The rebels immediately opened fire in response. The government forces, seeing that the rebels were unwilling to raise a white flag, continued to bomb the fortress. Mr. Mu announced tonight that he plans to continue appealing to the rebel leader tomorrow. (Guomin dispatch, 13th)

Dublin General Water Duffee, leader of the Irish Blue Shirts, announced today that two thousand Irishmen are not going to Spain to fight against communism. The date of their departure will not be announced for the time being. They will wear plain clothes and not carry weapons, so as not to violate the non-intervention agreement. Two representatives have already arrived at the headquarters of General Franco, leader of the Spanish rebel army, to discuss everything. (Reuters dispatch, 14th)

(Moscow) Women and children throughout the country are engaged in raising money and goods to support the women of the Spanish Republic. This is the first time the public has assisted the Spanish official army since Soviet Russia signed the non-intervention agreement in the Spanish Civil War. After textile workers in Moscow began to appeal, hundreds of female workers sent letters to the Moscow Pravda, many of which included donations. (Reuters dispatch, 14th)

Pope Speaks to Refugees - Condemns the Brutality of Civil War - Cultural Foundations Will Be Shaken

Castel Gandolfo The Pope spoke to five hundred Spanish refugees here today, broadcast by radio to Italy and other countries. In his account of the preparations by evil demons behind the Spanish Civil War, he condemned doctrines that destroy humanity, saying that the flames of hatred and persecution have re-ignited in Spain. Their purpose is to deal with the Catholic Church, because the Catholic Church is the only true obstacle to the exercise of destructive forces. This can be seen in countries such as Soviet Russia and Mexico. We must grieve for the violence of this fratricide, for the crimes against the Christian life and dignity, and for the destruction of the most sacred and precious traditions of a noble nation. The events in Spain have now reached the point where the foundations of all culture and civilization will be shaken. Those who destroy humanity are now seeking a common ground with Catholics. Their cunning schemes are extremely dangerous, and their aim is only to obscure the eyes and ears of the world. The Pope concluded by saying that he wished to pray that those who persecute the Church in Spain today will be reunited with the Church when peace is restored. (Reuters dispatch, 14th)

Vatican City Since the outbreak of civil strife in Spain, five hundred monks and ordinary people from that country have fled to Italy. They visited Pope Pius XI today. The Pope gave a speech to them, vehemently attacking communism, denouncing it as "devilish propaganda, the purpose of which is to conquer the whole world, so that it will be dominated by barren and harmful ideas. The party members of this evil force are trying in every way to get closer to Catholics, so as to cooperate with them, and thus facilitate the deception of Europe and the world, making them negligent in their defenses, and then taking the opportunity to achieve their private desires of hatred, rebellion, and destruction." (Havas dispatch, 14th)

(Paris) Observers here today believe that the Spanish Civil War will likely drag on until Christmas before a final victory can be determined. Conservatives estimate that 95,000 Spaniards have died in the civil strife so far, with an equal number wounded. There are still 20,000 prisoners in confinement, and property losses amount to approximately 10 billion Spanish pesetas. (Guomin dispatch, 13th)

Assassination Attempt on the British King – Masterminded by a Foreign Power – Perpetrator Sentenced to One Year Imprisonment

(London) The would-be assassin of the British King, McMahon, today made a shocking confession at the Old Bailey, stating that his attempt on the King's life was motivated by a foreign power that paid him for the task. He has now been sentenced to one year's imprisonment with hard labor. The courtroom was extremely crowded today for the hearing. The charges against McMahon totaled three: (1) Unlawfully possessing a weapon and attempting to endanger life; (2) Drawing a pistol while near the King, attempting to disturb the peace; (3) Unlawfully displaying a firearm with the intent to alarm the King. The most noteworthy event during today’s hearing was when McMahon stood to defend himself, admitting that in October 1935, he had been contacted by a certain foreign power and tasked with espionage. He further claimed that this foreign power provided him with money and the file number of documents he received, giving them to the War Office. This foreign representative attempted to incite him to rebel against the British government. A plan was then agreed upon to take advantage of the King's attendance at the Trooping the Colour ceremony in Hyde Park on July 16th and shoot him, for which he would be paid £150. It was also arranged to assign nine others to accompany him and assist in his escape. McMahon claimed to have reported this conspiracy to the War Office. McMahon also learned that if this conspiracy failed, they planned to attempt another assassination when the King visited France. When the case began, Attorney General Sir Thomas Inskip argued that the charges against the defendant were firmly established based on the previous evidence, and that there was no need to investigate the defendant's psychology regarding the third charge, or whether the King was alarmed. Mrs. Yaoman, residing in Leedon Street, testified in court that she had heard McMahon talking to a police officer by the roadside. As soon as their conversation ended, the royal procession from Hyde Park appeared. Mrs. Yaoman said, "I saw the King pause slightly to acknowledge the salute and look in the direction where McMahon was. I glanced back and saw McMahon raise his arm, and then I saw something fly from his hand and strike the King's horse." Upon questioning by the judge, Mrs. Yaoman agreed that it would not have been difficult for McMahon to fire a gun. She confirmed that McMahon had leaned over to throw the pistol. Special Constable Dix testified in court that he saw McMahon raise the gun to fire and immediately rushed forward, striking his hand and grabbing him, but did not see anything thrown from McMahon's hand. Constable Mabey testified, "At the time, I happened to be looking to the left when I saw McMahon rush towards the King. I went forward and seized him with both hands. I clearly saw a bright, shiny object fall beneath the feet of the King's horse." Firearms expert Churchill testified that McMahon's gun could easily fire five bullets in two seconds but could not confirm whether the gun had been used. McMahon's confession that he was paid by a foreign power to assassinate the King shocked everyone in the courtroom. When explaining why he carried the pistol, McMahon spoke in a low voice, stating that he knew his actions were extremely dangerous and felt uneasy, as he was both receiving money from a foreign power and reporting this information to the British government, which would inevitably lead to trouble. McMahon also wrote the names of the foreign embassy officials who had introduced him and those who had paid him to assassinate the King on a piece of paper, which he presented to the judge and prosecutor. McMahon added that the witnesses' statements were all accurate. He did not want to fire the gun at the time and so threw the pistol to the ground. The purpose of assassinating the King was to cause the disintegration of the British Empire, so that other countries could acquire its parts. When the prosecutor cross-examined McMahon, the defendant appeared extremely flustered and said, "I do not seek a pardon. I am merely revealing the whole truth and am willing to go to prison and suffer severe punishment, as only in prison can I escape the clutches of those I have deceived." The prosecutor questioned why McMahon had not revealed in the initial hearing that the letter to Home Secretary Simon had been instigated by a foreign spy. McMahon replied that his intention was to lure out all those involved in this conspiracy and that two foreign spies were eavesdropping in court when he testified in the police court. The prosecutor believed that McMahon's conspiracy was entirely a figment of his imagination. Upon hearing this, McMahon replied that only God knew the truth. McMahon's defense lawyer stated that although McMahon's confession was somewhat fanciful, it was not necessarily untrue. The Attorney General finally stated that McMahon's confession today was completely different from what he had said before in the police court. How could someone who disregarded oaths be trusted? Therefore, his words were unbelievable. The authorities have investigated McMahon's allegations of a conspiracy against the King, and the result has been to discover that his statements are completely unfounded. (Reuters, 14th)

(London) King Edward VIII, having departed from Dübendorf Airport in Switzerland aboard a royal aircraft, is hurrying back to the country, scheduled to arrive today. He is scheduled to proceed to Balmoral Castle in Scotland on the 19th of this month for hunting. There is a forest there that the King has rented for three weeks for the purpose of hunting. Furthermore, the White Star Line plans to build a large passenger ship of 81,000 tons, a sister ship to the "Queen Mary," and the keel will be laid soon. His Majesty will also visit to inspect the ship at that time. (Havas, 14th)

Joint Declaration of the Little Entente: Determined to Strengthen Security System with Force - Collective Security Not Limited to Europe - Recognizing Regional Treaties as Elements of Peace

Improvement in Sino-American Trade

(Washington) The U.S. Department of Commerce announced today that both imports and exports between China and the United States showed improvement in July. Exports to China totaled $4,845,000, compared to $2,251,000 during the same period last year. Imports from China totaled $6,672,000, compared to $6,261,000 during the same period last year. (National Telegram, 13th) The Standing Legal and Political Conference of the Little Entente in Bratislava, Czechoslovakia, continued its meeting this morning. After the meeting, a communiqué was issued, stating, "Czechoslovakia, Yugoslavia, and Romania have decided to unite all their forces to strengthen the security system." The policies to be pursued by the Little Entente are divided into four areas: (1) To work together and maintain solidarity, and to operate within the framework of the League of Nations despite the difficulties it has faced. Regional agreements are recognized as important elements of the peace situation. (2) The collective security system is not only applicable to Western Europe. (3) The Little Entente will maintain the most friendly relations with its neighboring countries. (4) The Little Entente will not interfere in the internal affairs of other countries, nor shall other countries interfere in the internal affairs of the Little Entente. The next meeting will be held in Geneva during the League of Nations conference. (Havas, 14th)

The Standing Political Conference of the Little Entente in Bratislava, Czechoslovakia, opened today and will conclude tomorrow evening, after which a communiqué will be issued. However, the Little Entente will reiterate the resolutions passed at the Standing Political Conference in May of this year (held in the Yugoslav capital) and the Heads of State Conference in June (held in the Romanian capital), especially the principle that negotiations on international treaties must be handled jointly by the Entente. At this moment, what is particularly emphasized by political figures is the agreement recently reached between Yugoslav Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Stojadinović and Romanian Prime Minister Tătărescu, stipulating that Romania should sell part of its oil production to Yugoslavia to be used for the latter's national defense plans. Those in charge say that the three Little Entente countries all want to strengthen the power of the League of Nations covenant and expand the content of regional security pacts. The appropriate measures to be taken in the event of violations of international treaties have also been carefully considered. In addition, Czech Prime Minister Hodža recently held talks with Yugoslav Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Stojadinović and Romanian Foreign Minister Antonescu outside the conference, discussing economic issues in the Danube region. (Havas, 13th)

International Commercial Telegram - September 14th, Reuters Special Commercial Intelligence

Gold and Silver

The price of gold in London today was 137 shillings and 5 pence, one penny lower than the closing price on Saturday.

London: The silver market today was calm and transactions were small. The spot and futures prices remained unchanged at 19 pence and 4375. Speculators bought in, while India sold out.

The silver market in Mountry remained very quiet today. The opening price for the November futures was 44.5144.84, the same as yesterday's closing price.

Exchange Rates

The London foreign exchange market was busy this morning, and the price of the pound was firm. The opening exchange rate between the British pound and the US dollar was $5.059375, higher than the US-British closing price on Saturday by .09375. After an hour, it continued to rise by .375. The rising trend continued before noon, and the price at 1 PM was $5.065, .5625 higher than the opening price. The opening price of the exchange rate between the British pound and the French franc was unchanged at 76.84. The franc weakened, and the exchange rate rose. The telegraphic rate was 76.93, higher by 9 pounds than the opening price.

Securities

The New York stock market was active this morning. The European situation continued to be serious. The elections in the Maine province and the lack of general excitement made merchants feel uneasy and forced them to sell. The prices of public utility, steel, and railway stocks fell sharply. Steel even fell by more than one dollar. Later, the prices of other stocks also fell one after another. The market was quite uneasy. Operators mostly took a wait-and-see attitude. Although there was a slight buying trend before noon, it was not enough to reverse the already declining market price. The selling pressure surged at noon, and market prices generally fell. However, public utility and oil stocks were able to maintain their stability in the midst of the difficult situation of these various securities. The amount by which railway, copper, and steel stocks fell was often between one and two dollars. The prices of public utility and automobile stocks fell by half a pound. The only highlight in the market was that oil stocks still had some buying interest. The market prices of New York stocks are listed below.

Cotton and Wheat

The Liverpool wheat market opened firmly, due to the slightly higher prices quoted by the traders on the Plata River in South America and some retail purchases from outside the industry. The high increase in weekly shipping figures caused recent prices to lag behind, while futures prices were resilient due to the hope for rain in the Southern Hemisphere. At 1 PM, the price for the October futures was 7 shillings and 7 pence and 625, an increase of .125 compared to the closing price on Saturday.

Liverpool cotton was slightly looser. At 1 PM, the price for the October futures was 6.63, a decrease of 2 pounds.

In Chicago this morning, the general interest in the wheat market was low, and the transactions were purely commercial in nature. The sentiment was still good, and the overall trend was upward. At the time of the telegram, the price for the December futures was 112.375, an increase of .25 compared to yesterday's closing price. Miscellaneous grains were slightly mixed, with fluctuations that were erratic and minimal. At noon, the price for the December futures was 93.75, a decrease of .25.

The New York cotton market opened in a mixed manner. Continued hedging limited transactions. The recent price was loose, while the futures price was slightly firmer due to slight purchases. Later, prices rebounded due to good buying sentiment, and good buying requests from the trade and foreign countries. At noon, the price for the December futures was 12.0, an increase of 3 pounds compared to yesterday's closing price.

Rubber

The London rubber market was stable today. At 1 PM, the transaction price for the October-December futures was 7 pence and 6875, the same as the closing price on Saturday. The New York rubber market was sluggish and uninteresting. The news was lacking and the fluctuations were narrow. The opening price for the December futures fell by 1 pound. Later prices stabilized. At noon, the price was 16.47, an increase of 1 pound compared to the closing price on Saturday. The market prices of New York goods are listed below.

Expansion of the Tianjin Japanese Consulate General: Eight Departments to Operate Starting Next Month - Plan to Increase Budget and Expand Police Powers

Tianjin Correspondence: The newly appointed Japanese Consul General in Tianjin, Kaneki Horiuchi, will have been in office for almost a week. The expansion of the Tianjin Consulate General, making it the central organization for diplomacy and economics among the Japanese consulates in North China, and the expansion of the police department and increasing the number of police officers, etc., has begun to be prepared based on instructions from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. Horiuchi was originally scheduled to fly to Shanghai on the 14th to meet Ambassador Kawagoe to request instructions regarding the implementation of this matter. However, because Kawagoe went to Beijing to negotiate on diplomatic matters, it has been postponed until Kawagoe returns to Shanghai next week. Regarding the expansion of the consulate general's organization, it has been decided to implement it in early October. In addition to Consul General Horiuchi, several new or changed personnel will be added to the consulate staff, making it a special organization for North China. Second Secretary Ogihara of the Shanghai Embassy has also been transferred to serve as the Tianjin Consul and will take office in early next month. Taniguchi, the current Vice Consul of the Tianjin Consulate, has been transferred to serve as the Vice Consul of Harbin. His vacancy will be filled by Vice Consul Tanaka, who is stationed in Nanjing, and he will also take office next month. The consulate general will be divided into eight departments: (1) General Affairs, (2) Foreign Affairs, (3) Investigation, (4) Economy, (5) Commerce, (6) Police Affairs, (7) Justice, (8) Personnel. The entire consulate has three consuls: Kiichi Anzai, Ogihara, and Murakami; and three vice consuls: Nishida, Nagai, and Tanaka. There are seven secretaries, including Hamada. Anzai and Nishida are in charge of the three departments of General Affairs, Foreign Affairs, and Personnel. Ogihara and Nagai are in charge of the departments of Commerce, Economy, and Investigation. Murakami and Tanaka are in charge of the departments of Justice and Police Affairs. Horiuchi is in charge of all of them. In addition to those serving in the consulate, several secretaries will be added and dispatched to Tangshan, Tanggu, Changli, Baoding, and Shijiazhuang to establish consular branch offices. According to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' plan, they will protect overseas Chinese and guide trade. Only the three branch offices currently established are Tanggu, Changli, and Tangshan. Baoding and Shijiazhuang will only be realized after the budget is approved next month due to budget constraints.

As for the establishment of the police department, the representatives of the three northeastern provinces decided on a plan at the meeting in Tianjin. After Administrative Officer Ota returned to the country to report, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs prepared a budget, intending to increase the annual reserve fund by 147,950 yuan starting in January of next year. At the same time, the expansion of police power in North China will be implemented. Currently, the Tianjin Consulate Police Station has a total of 110 police officers and patrols. After the expansion, it can be increased by two times compared to the current number. The existing police stations attached to the consulates in Qingdao, Jinan, Beiping, Taiyuan, Zhangjiakou, and the three railway lines of Pinghan, Beining, and Tianjin-Pukou, as well as the branch offices planned to be established, are all included and are directly under the jurisdiction of the Tianjin Police Department. Even the Gubeikou Independent Police Branch will be incorporated into the unified governance. After the unification of the command, the current Police Chief Kazuhisa, whose official rank is relatively low, will be transferred to serve domestically. A person of the "Police Inspector" rank will be dispatched to serve as the director. However, he will still be under the supervision and command of the Tianjin Consulate General. (14th)

Former Prime Minister Pan Fu Dies in Beiping

Beiping Correspondence: Former Prime Minister Pan Fu, after retiring from public office, resided in Tianjin and engaged in business ventures. In recent years, due to poor business performance, and last year the passing of his fifth concubine's son just two days after birth, Pan, overwhelmed by grief, contracted dysentery and pulmonary edema. This year, in June, he came to Beiping from Tianjin, residing at his residence in Maojiawan. After consulting Xiehe Hospital, he was diagnosed with cancerous pleurisy, deemed incurable. Later, he sought treatment from Dr. Lin Baoluo, who diagnosed him with right-sided suppurative pleurisy, with fluid accumulation for three months. His chest was severely affected, and the illness had been delayed. Drainage was attempted, but deemed too late. At that time, his breathing was rapid, with over thirty breaths per minute, and his pulse rate was over one hundred and twenty. His appetite sharply declined, sleep was restless, he was irritable and thirsty, sweated profusely, and urinated little. His heart and lungs were under extreme pressure, considered beyond the reach of medication. On June 25th, he was admitted to the German Hospital, but treatment was ineffective. He returned home. Three or four days ago, Pan contracted dysentery again, eventually succumbing to the illness, passing away at fifteen minutes past midnight on the twelfth. The encoffining took place at six o'clock in the afternoon. His concubine, Zhang, accompanied by his son, Yao Lin, and sons Sen, Tong, Nan, Qi, Xiang, Xing, and Ao, and four daughters attended by his side, grieving intensely. Pan's coffin is scheduled to remain at home for thirty-five days, after which it will be transported back to Jining, Shandong, for burial. Funeral arrangements are being handled by Political Committee members Liu Zhe and former Gendarmerie Commander Wang Qi. Pan's old friends Zhang Ting'e, Zhu Zuozhou, and Wu Qiufang also came from Tianjin to Beiping to assist in all matters. His family telegraphed Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, Zhang Xueliang, He Yingqin, Yan Xishan, Chen Tiaoyuan, and Yu Xuezhong to report the death, all of whom sent replies to Beiping to express condolences. Song Zheyuan, being in Tianjin, sent Qin Decun as his representative to pay respects.

According to someone at Pan's residence, around eleven o'clock on the morning of the eleventh, Shen suddenly said the air in the house was bad and instructed servants to move a chair to the courtyard. He was extremely thirsty and asked for tea. Shen suddenly fell into a coma and passed away around twelve o'clock at night. His fourth concubine, hearing of Pan's deteriorating condition, rushed from Tianjin to Beiping at ten o'clock on the evening of the eleventh, also bringing Pan's father's coffin. She met Pan but exchanged only a few words before their final farewell. When Pan's father's coffin was being made, Pan had said he wished to die in his father's place, sleeping in that coffin. Now his words had come true. Pan was quite lucid the day before his death. On the night of the tenth, he instructed his son, Yaoqi, to write his will to his family and letters to friends. His will stated, "I have been ill for years, and I have felt uneasy these past few days, fearing it is not a good sign. If anything untoward happens, you must take good care of your grandfather to avoid causing him grief. It is of utmost importance. Maintain the household and do not disgrace the family name. Living in North China, with such a state of affairs, weighs heavily on my mind, and I have nothing to contribute, for which I am truly ashamed. You should follow my aspirations, serve society, and strive to be upright people. Respect your elders, listen to their teachings, and obey their commands. Relatives, friends, and old subordinates should unite sincerely, help each other, and not betray my trust." The letters to friends were addressed to Song Zheyuan, Zhang Xueliang, Wu Peifu, Jin Yunpeng, Huang Fu, Wang Kemin, Liu Zhe, Ge Dingyuan, Wang Shuhan, and others. The letters stated, "I have been uneasy these past few days, fearing it is not a good omen. If I should not recover, I beg my brothers to kindly persuade my father to avoid causing him grief, which would slightly alleviate my guilt. My children are young; I hope you will instruct them. Cherish and support my old subordinates. Please settle any unfinished matters. This is my deepest prayer." Pan, during his lifetime, was fond of bronzes, stone inscriptions, calligraphy, and paintings, calling himself the Master of Huajian Pavilion. The origin of the name: (1) There are three versions of the Huashan Stele: the Huayin version, the Changyuan version, and the Siming version. Pan had already acquired three volumes. The Siming version was obtained for one hundred thousand gold pieces. The Huayin and Changyuan versions are housed in a foreign museum. (2) Pan possessed a Song Dynasty edition of the Zizhi Tongjian. Only one copy of this book exists in the country, hence Pan specifically took the two characters Huajian to name his pavilion. Last year, Pan had a life insurance policy worth thirty thousand yuan at a bank in Beiping. This money can be obtained to cover funeral expenses. (13th)

Strict Prohibition of Opium and Gambling in Chaozhou and Shantou; Offenders Severely Punished; Opium Addicts Given a Deadline to Register and Quit

Shantou Correspondence: Since the Guangdong Provincial Government implemented strict prohibitions on opium and gambling, all gambling dens in Shantou have closed down, and all gamblers employed by various companies have been dismissed. Restaurants, hotels, and brothels associated with gambling are desolate and unusually quiet. Prostitutes are relinquishing their licenses at the Flower Tax Bureau, and twenty to thirty people are moving to Hong Kong and Macau daily. After twelve o'clock at night, there is no noise, and law-abiding residents can sleep peacefully. The Shantou military police, to prevent unemployed gamblers from becoming bandits, patrol day and night to protect the city. Some shameless individuals, colluding with ruffians, are gambling Mahjong on the upper floor of a foreign firm in Yushan Street, complacent and thinking, "What the whole city cannot do, I alone can do." The sound of clacking tiles reverberates throughout the night, drawing glares from nearby residents, but the patrols can do nothing. The gamblers are taking it a step further, partnering with ruffians at a large hotel in Qilu to set up a major gambling den, complete with dancing, a bar, and opium smoking, possessing substantial capital and preparing for a grand opening. Gambling is extremely strictly prohibited in various parts of Chaozhou and Shantou. In Chao'an, employees of the Fengle Company were arrested by the police for playing Mahjong, each fined one thousand yuan. News of arrests and fines in other places is frequent. Gamblers are well aware that they must restrain themselves. The Shantou Municipal Government recently received orders to establish an Opium Prohibition Committee, to be established within the month. Three local individuals will be nominated as standing committee members, one serving as chairman, to handle daily affairs. The Provincial Opium Prohibition Committee will assign personnel to participate in guidance and supervision. After the Opium Prohibition Committee is established, it will set up opium cessation hospitals and clinics to assist opium addicts in quitting. All opium addicts in the city must register by the end of the year. Those under forty years of age are not allowed to register. Only those over forty years of age are allowed to register and be issued a license. Those under forty years of age must be admitted to the hospital for treatment, with a thirty-day deadline to quit and be discharged. Registration certificates will be issued bi-annually, with ordinary certificates costing five yuan per quarter and special certificates costing six jiao per quarter. Regarding party, government, military, financial, educational, and public officials and employees of various agencies who privately smoke opium, they must immediately quit within this month. If they privately smoke without reporting to their superiors, they will be punished according to law if discovered. Once the Opium Prohibition Committee is established, it will implement the central government's regulations on opium cessation and inspection, targeting civil servants of Shantou without leniency or pardon.

Opium Trafficking King of Northern Anhui, Qin Zixiu, Arrested in Bengbu; Accomplice Wang Congzhou Also Apprehended

Bengbu Correspondence: The poisonous atmosphere of opium in northern Anhui is pervasive, becoming more severe in recent years. Although the authorities have strictly enforced prohibition, the spread of opium has not diminished. The reason for this is the immersion and degradation of addicts, their stubbornness and inflexibility, and the secret trafficking and sale by treacherous individuals, which is the main factor in promoting the scourge of opium. The Public Security Bureau here recently arrested Qin Zixiu, a notorious wanted criminal known as the Opium King of Northern Anhui, and his accomplice Wang Congzhou, which has attracted considerable attention from the general public. According to investigations, Qin is originally from Suxian, a notorious scoundrel on the Huai River, with hundreds of followers, renowned in the Huai and Si regions. Younger members of the gang often call him "Young Master Qin." He roams the streets, committing numerous crimes, and he, along with the executed Zhu Yanqiu, Du Molin, and Chen Bingheng, were figures of concern to the Anhui provincial authorities. Last winter, the provincial government telegraphed the Bengbu Public Security Bureau, ordering his arrest and legal punishment. Qin, having heard the news, fled without a trace. This summer, he returned to Bengbu and was recently accused by eleven citizens, including Wu Huating, to the Public Security Bureau, leading to his arrest. According to Wu's accusations, which are based on documented facts, his notorious deeds are evident, and he is considered a public pest. The accusations include: (1) In 1925, during the time of the warlord Anwu Army, Qin served as a minor leader. While stationed at Linhuai Pass, he colluded with the bandit leader Zheng Yufang. Due to a dispute over the spoils, he secretly strangled the bandit and his wife, Zhu. He also colluded with the bandit leader Gong Huaiyin. In order to rob property, Qin, seeing the wealth, took advantage of his position and murdered Gong and his wife. (2) In 1926, Qin returned to Bengbu and became sworn brothers with Zhang Zonghan (also known as Zhang Dingchen), a notorious bandit from the northern countryside of Huaiyuan, engaging in numerous robberies. (3) In 1931, when the Seventh Division was stationed in Bengbu, suppressing bandits in Guzhen, seven bandits were captured and taken to the division headquarters in Southern Suzhou, claiming that Qin Zixiu, Zhang Dingchen, and Ma Xunchen were supplying them with firearms and ammunition. The Seventh Division Commander Wang Jun ordered the Twenty-first Brigade Commander Li Wenbin to arrest Qin in Sanyili, Bengbu, and escort him to the division headquarters in Southern Suzhou. Qin, being incredibly resourceful, was released with the help of gentry and merchants. (4) During the tenure of former Public Security Bureau Director Yun, Qin colluded with the bandit Lu Keqin, robbing in Shouchangli in this city, killing a patrol officer. Former Director Yun dispatched police to arrest Qin and send Lu Keqin for execution by firing squad. In addition, it was stated that Qin was wanted and arrested by Chairman Liu of the Provincial Government in 1935, avoiding arrest by fleeing elsewhere, and recently returning to Bengbu to sell opium, known as the Opium King of Northern Anhui, a widely known reputation, recruiting hundreds of followers, including Wang Congzhou, as his henchmen, acting solely under Qin's command. Public Security Bureau Director Lu Zongjing reported this and, on the night before last, sent officers along with armed police to arrest Qin Zixiu and Wang Congzhou at their residences. Yesterday (the 12th), they were transferred to the Fengyang County Government for legal action. Locals generally agree that the case should be severely punished to eliminate harm to the people. The authorities may impose the death penalty.

Jing-Qu Railway Changes Route, Abandoning the Quzhou Section in Zhejiang, Extending from Xuancheng to Guixi

Wuhu Correspondence: The Ministry of Railways' construction of the Jing-Qu Railway originally planned to start from Quzhou in Zhejiang and Xuancheng in Anhui, with Xuancheng connecting to the Jiangnan Railway's Xuanwu section of the Jiangnan Company, allowing it to reach Nanjing via Wuhu and the Jingwu section. The entire route was 350 kilometers long. In July, the Engineering Bureau was established in Xuancheng, with Zheng Hua as the Director and Yuan Menghong as the Chief of Engineering. Construction began immediately. Recently, after careful inspection by the Ministry of Railways, it was deemed necessary to modify the route. It has been decided to abandon the Quzhou section in Zhejiang and extend directly south from Xuancheng to Jiangxi, passing through Ningguo, Qimen, Jingdezhen, Leping, and ending at Guixi, extending the length to 400 kilometers. Although this plan has not been officially announced, over 5,000 workers originally in Zhejiang have been transferred back to Anhui. It is estimated that a total of 14 million cubic meters of earthwork is required for the entire route. For land requisitioned from civilians, the price is divided into three grades: 30 yuan, 20 yuan, and 10 yuan per mu. The cost of moving graves is also stipulated at 5 yuan. A total of over 900,000 railway ties are required. To promote domestically produced timber, it was decided to procure locally produced chestnut trees from Ningguo and Qimen counties along the route, as tie material, in consultation with the Anhui Provincial Government. The Provincial Government welcomed this and established the Anhui Province Domestic Timber Sales Office within the Wuhu Engineering Bureau to liaise with timber merchants in each county, responsible for contracting. The first batch of 60,000 ties has been contracted for procurement, with each tie costing only 2 yuan in legal tender, saving much compared to imported products. Therefore, it is planned to increase this amount gradually in the future. The entire route is expected to be completed and open to traffic by the end of next year. The work is being carried out simultaneously in sections, with nearly 15,000 to 16,000 workers. The steel rails will be 70 pounds in weight. The locomotive budget requires over 20 locomotives. It is heard that the Ministry of Railways' Materials Purchasing Committee is preparing to place an order with Britain due to the Boxer Indemnity funds. The total cost of construction is estimated at 30 million yuan. The agricultural produce in southern Anhui and the border of Jiangxi is extremely abundant, but transportation has always been inconvenient. After the completion of this route, it will connect with the Jiangnan Railway to reach Nanjing and connect with the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, which will connect with the Guangdong-Hankou Railway, achieving satisfactory results in both freight and passenger transport. (13th)

Songjiang: Water Patrol Secretly Arrests Suspected Thieves

Fei Gongxia, the captain of the Water Patrol Team of the local Public Security Bureau, conducted a rendezvous patrol in Fengjing yesterday and discovered two suspicious individuals in the town. He immediately went forward to question them. A six-inch Browning pistol, number 398, was found in Wang A'gen's crotch. His companion, Zhang Zixian, also known as Zhang Jinlong, nicknamed Zhang Mulong, was evasive and clearly not a good person. They have been taken in for questioning.

Taicang: Child Crushed to Death by Fallen Ginkgo

Outside the East Gate, inside the Land Temple, there are several large ginkgo trees that bear abundant fruit every year, contracted out by villagers. This year, He Haibao from Xinfeng Township contracted it. Yesterday, while collecting the fruit, they used bamboo poles to knock them down, instructing nearby village children to pick them up, paying them four copper coins for each full basket. As the fruit on the top of the tree could not be knocked down, He climbed to the top of the tree. While working, a large branch suddenly broke and fell to the ground, instantly crushing Chen Tianxiong and Chen Runsheng to death. Their flesh and blood were blurred beyond recognition, a tragic sight. He and several lightly injured children were taken to the bureau for investigation.

Changshu: Another Case of Grain Tax Embezzlement Discovered

The West Counter Grain Tax Office of the County Government has recently discovered another case of tax corruption. The perpetrator is the younger brother of Zhou Zhiyun, the head of the counter. He has been detained and imprisoned. Last month, the Grain Tax Office discovered that an employee, Zhou Jianwo, had forged grain certificates and privately collected national taxes. This has now been verified. He has been sentenced to three years imprisonment and is in jail. Unexpectedly, internal opinions have arisen among internal employees, because someone secretly reported the internal corruption to the Finance Department, which sent Chen to Changshu to investigate. It was discovered that Zhou Ruizhi, an employee of the counter, had privately collected taxes from a Jiang family noodle shop in the alley, secretly embezzling them for many years. Commissioner Chen has now found evidence and immediately arrested and imprisoned Zhou Ruizhi. At the same time, all old certificates from the West Counter have been sealed to facilitate a thorough investigation. It is reported that Zhou Ruizhi, the perpetrator of this embezzlement, and the already imprisoned forger of grain certificates, are both younger brothers of the current head of the West Counter, Zhou Zhiyun.

Suzhou: Three Villages Robbed in a Row in Weiting Township

During this time when new grains are being harvested in the countryside, bandits are taking the opportunity to be active, leading to frequent robberies in recent days. Although the authorities have tried their best to search, the bandits move about, making it difficult to pacify the situation. The other day, Weiting Township reported a bandit alarm. Three villages were robbed in a single night. That evening, more than ten bandits, wearing short gray clothes, speaking with a Hakka accent, their faces painted, and their heads wrapped in white cloth, first robbed Zhu Shoufu and Zhang Fuxiang's families in Jinsha East Henggang, then robbed Zhang Zhucun's and Yu Jinfu's families in Wenchao West Zhang Village and Guapeng, taking away a new boat before leaving. Unexpectedly, when the bandits passed through the affluent Zuanzhu Village, they went to Li Houfu's house and ransacked it, then fled west. The next day, the victims reported to the Weiting Fifth Precinct, which dispatched police to pursue them. At the same time, the Public Security Bureau was requested to send additional police to the countryside to investigate and arrest them based on the information.

Bandits Extort Doctor

Gu Dingyun, a doctor from Zhongzheng, Huguan, has a clinic in the town and a branch clinic at Bai Mu Bridge in Suzhou. Gu's family is moderately well-off, attracting the attention of bandits. Recently, someone, pretending to be a patient, asked him to go to the countryside to treat an illness. Unexpectedly, there was no patient when he arrived. Then he received a threatening letter from someone calling himself the First Army of Taihu Lake, extorting 2,000 yuan, to be delivered at the Wenchang Temple on the 12th. Gu reported this to the police station, which sent police to wait. As a result, only two suspects were apprehended. The search is still ongoing.

Wuxi: Election Ballot Counting in Wuxi

The matter of the election of national representatives from agricultural, industrial, commercial, and professional groups in Wuxi was completed on the 12th and 13th with the respective election of candidates in various rural areas, parks, and the county government. It is reported that there were 29 industrial groups with 222 votes and 63 trade associations with 661 votes participating. In addition, six trade associations, including entertainment, coal, construction, photography, flour mills, and Yao Huo, were not allowed to vote by provincial telegram because they had not joined the Chamber of Commerce. After these associations requested the Chamber of Commerce to temporarily join and participate in the vote, a telegram was submitted to the province for approval. Consequently, 48 votes were cast at the county government on the afternoon of the 13th. The ballot boxes from the eight counties in the Second District were sent to the district on the evening of the 13th. District Supervisor Zang Qifang ordered the counting to begin at 8:00 a.m. yesterday (the 14th), divided into two sessions: the first session for professional groups, the second session for commercial groups, and the third session for industrial groups. The ballot counting was carried out in the order of Wuxi, Wuxian, Wujin, Changshu, Wujiang, Jiangyin, Taicang, and Kunshan. Due to the non-participation of the Wuxian Farmers' Association, the number of votes was relatively small. The results of the ballot counting are as follows: (1) In industrial groups, Wuxi and Suzhou had the most votes, Jiangyin, Wujin, and Changshu followed, while Kunshan only had six votes. Taicang (seven votes) and Wujiang (no votes) were all invalid. As a result, Sun Xiangfeng, Xu Chiyu, and Tang Pu'an received the most votes, followed by Zhang Gongren, Zhang Jiesheng, Wu Yunyi, Chen Changgeng, and Gui Wuchen. (2) In commercial groups, Xue Mingjian, Qian Sunqing, Zhang Shoupeng, Yin Zhongren, Jiang Weixian, Yu Xunlu, Pang Shusen, Yu Xiaochuan, Yan Huiyu, Cheng Ganqing, Ding Zhixiang, and Lan Bohua received more votes. The above is the ballot counting for Wuxi County. It was completed at 4:30 p.m. More details will follow. (3) For agricultural groups, only Wuxi County has been counted, with Cheng Yicheng and Jiang Bosen receiving the most votes.

Pagoda Lantern on Jiangjian Ridge

Outside the North Dipper of this city, on Jiangjian Ridge, there is the tradition of piling Pagoda Lanterns every year on the 30th of the seventh month of the lunar calendar. This year, in front of Jiang Renmao's pottery shop, over two thousand earthenware basins were used to pile a Pagoda Lantern, a total of seven stories. The entire pagoda was decorated with over two thousand colorful electric lights. To the east of the pagoda, over twenty light sheds and two colorful arches were built. It was lit up last night, attracting crowds of viewers, a lively scene, the grandest in over ten years.

Yangzhou: Three Points for Careful General Election

Wang Xingfu, Lin Zhiting, and Lu Jia of the Jiangdu First District, Wu Yangchen of the Qing Dynasty, Wang Zaishan of the Fourth District, Ji Nuo of the Fifth District, Liu Bingqian, Gao Puqing, and Sang Xiaochu of the Eighth District, have issued a notice to all citizens of the county for the sake of a cautious general election of national representatives. The general idea is that there are three points to be cautious about in this general election: (1) Be cautious about the recommendation of the candidate. Can he be our representative and cope with everything in the present era? (2) Be cautious about the candidate's scholarship. Can he be our representative, benefiting the country above and benefiting the people below? (3) Be cautious about the current position of the candidate. Is he seeking wealth and strength for the country and relieving the suffering of the people?

Jiaxing: Button Factory Employee Commits Suicide

Yin Guoquan, a partner at the Lijia Button Factory in Jiaxing Tang, (23 years old, from Kunshan, Jiangsu,) had been studying at the factory for over eight years. He quit for some reason in July last year. He rejoined the factory in January this year. At the beginning of this month, he went to Bengbu to handle raw materials and returned on the 10th. He stayed at the Tianhu Hotel on Jianqiao Street that night. On the 11th, he went to the factory, and on the 12th, he left the factory again. He stayed at the Quanhu Hotel that night. For unknown reasons, he bought a small bottle of poison and, at night, wrote seven suicide notes and took the poison. At about 5 a.m. on the 13th, he called out with abdominal pain. The tea boy heard him and entered, finding him unconscious. There was a bottle of poison and suicide notes on the table. Knowing that he had taken poison, he informed the Guanyinkai police station, who sent a chief officer to the scene. Yin was sent to the Gospel Hospital for treatment, but his internal organs were already necrotic, and he could not be saved. He died at about 7 a.m. The Public Security Bureau reported to the local court for an autopsy. Qian Fanfang, the manager of the button factory, assigned employee Zhou Songlin to the scene to prepare a coffin and collect the body. The suicide notes have been distributed separately. According to the suicide notes, the reason for the suicide was due to the oppression of a bad environment. His brother-in-law, Tian Shengrong, from the north, will come to collect the coffin and transport it back for burial.

Haizhou: Wasteland Reclaimed for Cotton Planting

The Great School Field in this county, totaling 70 hectares, was previously occupied by the Tonghai Reclamation and Pasture Company. It was not reclaimed as a school field until 1928 and has been left barren as pastureland. The county education agency only leases it out for 200 yuan per year, with the lessee harvesting reeds. Now, locals, including Li Changming, have leased the school field. Based on the principle of making the best use of the land and resources, they have formulated a ten-year plan to start reclaiming the land for cotton planting and livestock raising. The term is ten years. The first year's rent is 200 national currency, increasing annually thereafter. Upon expiration, the school field will be taken back by the county government. Yesterday, they submitted a document along with the plan to the county government for transfer to the Department of Education for record, to show their sincerity.

Pests Devour Autumn Beans

In the southeast districts of Moyang County, due to continuous rain and flooding, the autumn harvest is hopeless. The autumn beans in districts 1, 2, 3, 4, and 10 are still lush, which is very gratifying to the farmers. Recently, bean worms (commonly known as bean dans) have been found in the fields, eating the bean leaves and multiplying rapidly. They are everywhere in the fields. The worms are yellowish-green and wriggle in the branches and leaves, like silkworms. Each autumn bean plant has dozens of them. The bean leaves are eaten, the branches and stems wither and become bare, and they do not bear fruit. The farmers are extremely anxious and flock to the fields to catch them and feed them to pigs. The worm oil can also be used for lighting. In recent days, the country lanes have been filled with them. If this continues for another half month, the autumn beans in each township will be completely devoured. It is hoped that the agricultural authorities will quickly organize a large-scale capture or offer to buy them, which may still provide a slight remedy and prevent recurrence next year.

Shaoxing: Husband Killer Sentenced to Imprisonment

Chen Zhangshi, a Shaoxing Tangpu villager, was found to have conspired with her lover, Chen Sifang, and her older brother, Zhang Changshan, to kill her husband, Chen Xiaoquan, with green wooden sticks in July. After the discovery, the Tangpu police station arrested the adulterous woman, Chen Zhangshi, and sent her to the court for trial. Chen Sifang and others are still at large. The court has now completed its investigation of the adulterous woman and sentenced her to nine years of imprisonment.

Hangzhou-Caoe Road Construction Postponed

The construction of the Hangzhou-Caoe section of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway was originally scheduled to begin on October 1st. However, the town leaders of Changan Town and others have submitted requests to the county government to transfer the request to the engineering office to postpone the start of construction for three weeks to protect the rice harvest. It is now heard that the engineering office has approved a postponement of twenty days, setting the start date for October 21st.

Xiaoshan: 100,000 Sandbank Residents Petition

Over 100,000 sandbank residents in eastern Xiaoshan, whose original sandbank land was sold by the Sandbank Bureau to new owners, causing the farmers, who survived the disaster, to have no way to appeal. After Magistrate Li took office, over four thousand farming households in Nansha, Zheshan, petitioned the county, and directly telegraphed the provincial and central governments, requesting the revocation of the order, and immediately inviting the original owners to pay the land price, the original owners should have priority, so that the landowners don't exploit and benefit, and maintain the lives of farmers. It is believed that the provincial and county authorities will approve their request.

Zhu Peide Arrives in Shanghai to Mediate the Situation in Guangxi; Bai Chongxi Decides to Serve in Nanjing; Ju Zheng and Others to Return North in a Week

Chief of Staff Zhu Peide was dispatched to the south last month to mediate the situation in Guangxi. He completed his mission some days ago and returned north on the President Jackson of the Dollar Steamship Lines from Hong Kong. He arrived in Shanghai at approximately 11 a.m. on the 14th, mooring at Buoys 13 and 14 in the Huangpu River. Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Songhu Garrison Commander Yang Hu, and Garrison Headquarters Secretary Wang Zhinan and others went to welcome him. After disembarking, Zhu immediately transferred to the Jingguang launch and crossed the river. At 11:40 a.m., he landed at the Xin Guan wharf and went directly to his private residence on Bi Xun Road to rest. Yang Hu was scheduled to host a welcome dinner for Zhu at the International Hotel at 7:30 p.m. on the 14th. Zhu plans to stay in Shanghai briefly before returning to Nanjing to assume his duties. According to Zhu, the Guangxi situation has been completely resolved, and the aftermath is currently being handled within Guangxi Province. Bai Chongxi is scheduled to go to Guangzhou within the next few days to pay his respects to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. Bai had originally intended to go abroad for inspection, but after Chiang Kai-shek's earnest persuasion, he has abandoned his plans to go abroad and has decided to serve in Nanjing. As to whether he will accompany Chairman Chiang north immediately after arriving in Guangzhou is yet to be determined. President Ju and others are scheduled to return north in a week. Regarding the Beihai Incident and the disposition of the 19th Route Army, he has not heard anything about them since leaving Guangzhou nearly a week ago. He plans to stay in Shanghai for a day or two before returning to Nanjing to assume his duties.

Lu Zuofu Discusses Sichuan Province's Construction, Negotiates Public Bond Mortgages, and Overcomes Reasons for Failure

Lu Zuofu, Director of the Sichuan Provincial Department of Construction, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning to host guests on the maiden voyage of the Minsheng Company's new ship, the "Minben". He personally received guests aboard. Therefore, he is committed to overcoming these reasons for failure in the construction of Sichuan Province, making thorough preparations first, and then proceeding with the work, in order to achieve success in one stroke.
