Minsheng Company Hosts Visit Yesterday; "Minben" Ship Makes Maiden Voyage Today

Over a Thousand Guests are Invited, Impressed by Elegance; Cargo Holds and Passenger Cabins Have Distinctive Features; Receptions Offered at Various Ports Along Chongqing Route

The "Minben" ship, built by the Minsheng Industrial Company, is the first fast, large ship on the Yangtze River. It departs today on its maiden voyage to Chongqing. Yesterday, from 1 p.m. to 5 p.m., at the Minsheng Wharf in Nanshi (i.e., Wharves 11 and 12), guests were invited to visit. The details are as follows:

Attentive Hospitality

The "Minben" ship was docked at Wharf 11 in Nanshi. Yesterday at 1 p.m., the entire ship was adorned with flags of various nations. Lu Zuofu, Director of the Sichuan Provincial Department of Construction and General Manager of Minsheng Industrial Company, Zheng Bicheng, Director of the Ship Department of the Minsheng General Company, Zhang Shulin, Manager of Minsheng Shanghai, and all the employees of Minsheng were on board to welcome guests. Over a thousand people, including Du Yuesheng, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Sheng Pingru, Xu Zufan, Zhu Ziqiao, and Li Zhiyi, were in attendance. They were first guided on a tour and then invited to the fourth floor for refreshments. The event ended at 5 p.m.

Ship Structure The "Minben" ship was built by the Jiangnan Shipyard. It is 221 feet long, 33 feet wide, 11.5 feet deep, and has a draft of 9.5 feet. It has a horsepower of 2,500 and can travel 16.17 nautical miles per hour. It uses a double-bottom hull and has six large cargo holds and eight tung oil tanks. It can carry 3,000 bales of cotton yarn and 180 tons of tung oil. The stern rudder adopts a streamlined design, making it slightly curved and rounded, which is an innovation for ships on the upper Yangtze. The most special feature is that the bow has two 15-ton cranes. The bow is over 70 feet long, and the middle hold is over 80 feet long. The bottom of the hold is paved with rails, as the company plans to transport railway cars and locomotive railway materials for the Chongqing-Chengdu Railway in the future. Therefore, it has designed and built this large ship suitable for transportation needs. From now on, there will be no problems transporting all kinds of iron bars and steel parts into Sichuan. The ship's engine was purchased from Socony's Yangtze River ship, and the cost of the hull and other materials still amounted to 500,000 yuan, the same as its sister ship, the "Minyuan". The ship is currently insured for 450,000 yuan. Excluding a 10% self-insurance, the remaining 90% is underwritten by various Chinese and foreign insurance companies in Shanghai.

Passenger Cabin Facilities

Location and facilities of passenger cabins: (1) Special-class cabins are located at the rear of the third floor. There are five rooms, each with two berths, accommodating a total of ten people. The beds use springs, and the mattresses are made of Simmons. There are wardrobes and new-style washbasins. There is a corridor in the middle leading to the dining room. The corridor has a skylight. Each room and dining room is sealed with plywood and painted with artistic lacquer. The facilities are complete and luxurious. There are also two bathrooms and toilets. The kitchen has an electric refrigerator that can make 200 pounds of ice every day, keeping food fresh and hygienic. There are tables and chairs behind the dining room for cooling off and viewing the scenery. (2) Official cabins are located at the front of the third floor. There are seven rooms, five with double berths and two with single berths, accommodating a total of twelve people. Most official cabins on other ships have stacked berths, which are inconvenient to climb up and down. This ship uses single berths and has cotton mattresses, which are extremely comfortable. The dining room is in the center and has a skylight, imitating the style of the special-class cabins. It is spacious and comfortable, cool in summer and warm in winter, making it the best among all Yangtze River ships. The dining room has two "dou" openings leading to the front corridor, making it very convenient for viewing the scenery and cooling off. There is also a bathroom and toilet. (3) Room cabins are located at the front of the first floor. There are five rooms, each with four berths, accommodating a total of twenty people. There is one dining room and two bathrooms and toilets. Most room cabins on other ships are located next to the boiler room or engine room, where the temperature is quite high. In summer, it is unbearable for passengers. This ship is located above the cargo hold, completely eliminating this problem. Because the dining room is in the front of the ship, it is cooler. (4) Third-class cabins are located at the rear of the second floor. There are five rooms, each with sixteen berths, accommodating a total of eighty people. There are four men's toilets, two men's showers, and one women's shower and toilet. The third-class cabins on this ship are simply an enlargement of the room cabins. The berths are comfortable, and the air circulates well. The space between the berths is wide, making traffic convenient. Tables can also be set up for meals. Third-class cabins are comfortable and have bathrooms, which is a unique feature of the company's ships. There are two large luggage rooms on both sides of the boiler room, surrounded by iron bars, making it easy to store luggage. (5) All classes of passenger cabins have heating facilities, so it is not cold even in severe winter. The stern of the fourth floor and the rooftop garden are available for cooling off and taking walks in the summer. Other amenities include electric fans and doorbells, multiple bathrooms and toilets, clean drinking water, a library for borrowing books, a radio receiver to announce important news from various ports, and musical instruments and entertainment to alleviate the loneliness of long journeys, all of which make passengers feel convenient.

Cargo Hold Features The bow of this ship is over 70 feet long and can accommodate 15 cars. The cargo hold openings are particularly large, and the bottom of the hold is paved with rails, which can accommodate locomotives and other heavy machinery. There is also a refrigerated hold at the stern, which can hold five tons of fresh goods. This is also not available on other ships on the Yangtze River. Regarding the safety of the ship, the hull of this ship is sturdy, the materials are the best, the design is excellent, and the layout is appropriate. The forward hold also has a double bottom, providing the best safety guarantee. In addition to the various fire safety equipment on the deck, the cargo hold also has steam fire extinguishing pipes to prevent fire alarms, which is not available on any Chinese or foreign ships on the Yangtze River. The ship travels steadily and quickly. The speed of this ship is 16.17 miles per hour, setting a new record for commercial ships on the Yangtze River. It only takes eight or nine days to go from Shanghai to Chongqing, and only five or six days to go from Chongqing to Shanghai. Other ships on the Yangtze River have not been able to combine stability and speed, but this ship has both. After numerous tests by Chinese and foreign experts, it is considered to be very satisfactory and perfect, truly a blessing for the shipping industry.

Departure for Chongqing Today

The "Minben" ship departs on its maiden voyage to Chongqing today. On the first voyage today, the income from freight alone loaded in Shanghai amounts to more than 60,000 yuan, not including passenger fares. The captain of the ship is Zhou Haiqing (formerly the captain of the "Minquan" ship), the manager is Xie Sasheng, the first mate is Yin Pingzhi, the second mate is Yao Weilin, and the chief engineer is Xu Jiatang. The ticket prices are lower than those of British Jardine Matheson and Swire. From Shanghai to Chongqing, a special-class Western meal costs 200 yuan per person, a special-class Chinese meal costs 160 yuan per person, a second-class ticket costs 70 yuan per person, and a third-class ticket costs 35 yuan per person. The ports of call along the ship's route are Shanghai, Nanjing, Hankou, Yichang, Wanxian, and Chongqing. According to Manager Zhang of the Shanghai branch, the "Minben" and "Minyuan" are sister ships. When there is flooding on the Yangtze River, they specialize in the Shanghai-Chongqing route. When the water level is low, they specialize in the Shanghai-Yichang route. The "Minben" ship is scheduled to make its maiden voyage from Shanghai to Chongqing on the evening of the 15th and plans to invite visitors to visit it when passing through Nanjing, Hankou, Yichang, and Wanxian. The "Changyuan" ship is expected to be completed in about a week and will join the Shanghai-Chongqing route.

Continuing to Build Seven Ships

The Minsheng Company has now become the only major company in the river shipping industry. It has a total of ten routes, including Chongqing-Shanghai, Chongqing-Yichang, Shanghai-Yichang, Chongqing-Hankou, Chongqing-Xuzhou, Xuzhou-Jialing, Luzhou-Deng, Chongqing-Fuling, Fuling-Wanxian, and Chongqing-Taizhou. It uses 45 ships, including the "Minyuan," "Minben," "Minquan," "Minfeng," "Minzhi," "Minsu," and "Minyi" to regularly run the Shanghai-Chongqing route, and the "Minzu," "Minlian," "Guangyao," and three other ships regularly run the Shanghai-Yichang route. The company is now taking another step forward and is building seven new Yangtze River ships in Shanghai, ranging in length from 150 feet to 170-180 feet. The drawings and costs have been submitted by the shipyard to the company for review in preparation for construction.

Rickshaw Pullers' Representatives Petition; Demand that the Municipal Council Maintain the Number of Rickshaws; Replace the Mutual Aid Society and Abolish Quotas

According to the Xinsheng News Agency, rickshaw pullers in the Special District, in protest of the Municipal Council's reduction of rickshaws, dispatched over three hundred people, including Chen Guobiao, Lu Shaode, Chen Hongji, Yu Baohe, Qian Youfu, Chen A'er, He Jintao, Xu Zhaoyuan, He Shunhou, Yang Agou, Lu Yinsheng, and Xia Qiyun, to the Municipal Council yesterday morning at 10 a.m. Because of the large number of people, they were stopped by police. They then publicly elected Chen Guobiao and seven others to see the Chief Executive. The Chief Executive was out, so they were received by General Manager Feixin Dun. Because of the language barrier, He Dekui was asked to translate. After inquiring about the petitioners' intentions, he individually questioned Lu Shaode, Ka Zhangfa, and others about how much they had left over each day after paying rent. The rickshaw pullers replied that due to the sluggish market, they only had 40-50 cents left, which was not enough to cover expenses. He asked the rickshaw pullers whether they thought it was better to have more rickshaws or fewer. They replied that because of rural bankruptcy, villagers came to Shanghai to make a living, so it was better to have more rickshaws so that they could be distributed to maintain their livelihoods. Mr. He also asked whether registered rickshaw pullers should be limited in number or not. The rickshaw pullers replied that not limiting the number would reduce the unemployed population. Mr. He replied that the petition would be translated and submitted to the Chief Executive for consideration. He also said that the Municipal Council's Rickshaw Special Committee and the Municipal Council's Huang Affairs Committee would hold meetings to discuss the rickshaw pullers' demands and promised to consider them. The representatives were satisfied and left. The text of their petition is as follows: "Petition Regarding: We, Chen Guobiao, Lu Shaode, Chen Hongji, Yu Baohe, Qian Youfu, Chen A'er, and others, the General Representatives of Rickshaw Pullers in the Special District, have been making a living by pulling rickshaws in Shanghai for many years. Unexpectedly, in 1934, the Public Concession Municipal Council, under the pretext of improving the lives of rickshaw pullers, arbitrarily reformed the rickshaw pulling system, established a Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Society, and extracted 15,000 yuan of blood and sweat from us rickshaw pullers every month for the Municipal Council personnel to squander. Although it is called relief, in fact, the rickshaw pullers do not get any benefit at all. Now that the Mutual Aid Society has been established for 26 months, it has absorbed as much as 390,000 yuan of our rickshaw pullers' blood and sweat. All matters are handled like a monopoly. It shouts loudly to provide relief to rickshaw pullers, but it is truly irrelevant to the rickshaw pullers themselves. Therefore, it must be fundamentally reorganized. We rickshaw pullers in Shanghai have never been subject to any restrictions and have been free to come and go. Since the Municipal Council started registering rickshaw pullers, we have been constantly interfered with by patrolmen, who strictly check our armbands and photos, making it impossible to maintain our business and causing us great pain. Moreover, your Council has implemented a quota system for registration, causing unemployed rickshaw pullers to wander aimlessly and unable to make a living, which is not a sincere intention to fundamentally improve and relieve rickshaw pullers. Recently, we have repeatedly seen reports that the Rickshaw Committee has proposed to your Council to reduce the number of public rickshaws in the Concession, cutting off the livelihood of us poor rickshaw pullers. If this is implemented, we rickshaw pullers in Shanghai will swear to resist it to the death. You must know that reducing one rickshaw means cutting off the livelihood of four rickshaw pullers, and so on. We believe that your Council does not understand the national conditions of our country and acts rashly, which is tantamount to cutting off toes to fit the shoes, and is greatly contrary to the system of relieving rickshaw pullers and improving their lives. Based on the opinions of the majority of rickshaw pullers, Guobiao and others convened an emergency meeting of rickshaw puller representatives from five districts on the afternoon of the 7th of this month. The resolutions are as follows: (1) Reorganize the Mutual Aid Society in the shortest possible time, and order the monopolizing personnel to thoroughly publish the accounts from the past. The affairs of the society should be returned to the management of both labor and management of the rickshaw industry in order to seek thorough and appropriate relief. (2) Abolish the quota for rickshaw puller registration and establish a permanent rickshaw puller registration office to relieve unemployed rickshaw pullers. (3) Cancel the proposal to reduce the number of rickshaws in order to avoid increasing unemployed rickshaw pullers and to maintain the business of those with rickshaws in order to save the actual livelihood of rickshaw pullers. The above is submitted to your Council for review and acceptance. We will be extremely grateful and await orders. Submitted to the Chief Executive of the Public Concession Municipal Council."

Sir Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen, the newly appointed British Ambassador to China, along with his family, arrived in Shanghai by ship at 1 p.m. on the 14th. A copy of the credentials will be sent to Nanjing first. Mr. Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen plans to inspect embassy affairs in Nanjing after presenting his credentials. Mr. Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen does not plan to socialize with officials in Shanghai before going to Nanjing.

Municipal Council Reduces Rickshaws; Citizens Oppose

The Needs of Citizens and Livelihood of Rickshaw Pullers Should be Considered; Public Bus Routes Should be Restricted

According to the Xinsheng News Agency, the Public Concession Municipal Council has proposed to reduce the number of public rickshaws. Rickshaw owners and pullers, because it is a matter of vital interest to them, have held meetings one after another to firmly oppose it. Various citizens' groups in the city, for the sake of convenient transportation, have also successively issued declarations, listing the impropriety of reducing the number of rickshaws. The original text is as follows: "The Public Concession Municipal Council has recently proposed to reduce the number of public rickshaws in the Concession in order to regulate traffic. As representatives of the citizens, our association believes that we cannot remain silent. In recent years, the expansion, extension, and addition of roads in the Public Concession have not kept pace with the increase in public bus routes. As it stands, the roads are often crowded with pedestrians, and on roads less than 30 feet wide, public buses as wide as 10 feet and as high as 25 feet travel back and forth, such as the No. 1, No. 5, and No. 15 public buses that pass through Henan Road, Datong Road, Nanjing Road, and North Sichuan Road. This has a significant impact on municipal traffic, pedestrian safety, and obstructing advertisements and business along the road. For the sake of the municipality and for the sake of commerce, the Municipal Council should restrict the route and number of public buses in order to benefit the citizens. This is one point. In fact, due to the different economic needs of Chinese and foreign citizens in the Public Concession, Westerners live in foreign houses along Jing'an Temple Road and the areas outside the concession. Cars can reach their doors directly, so most of them have cars for transportation and do not worry about the number of public rickshaws. For Westerners, the amount of rickshaws may not have much of an effect on transportation, but the more than one million Chinese in the Concession are limited by their economic ability. The number of people who own cars is very small. The majority of Chinese rely on rickshaws as their only means of transportation, and public buses cannot reach the remote streets and lanes where they live. Without rickshaws for transportation, the more than one million Chinese in the Concession would feel greatly inconvenienced. For the sake of Chinese convenience, the Municipal Council should not reduce the number of public rickshaws in order to benefit the citizens. This is the second point. Moreover, looking at the traffic management policies of major cities in Europe and the United States, the development of electric and steam transportation businesses in major cities is usually expanded beyond the road surface to the air or the ground. For example, in New York in the United States, in addition to public buses and trams on the road surface, there are also elevated and underground trams. Each vehicle does not run on the same road to avoid traffic congestion. In contrast, in our city, Nanjing Road, Avenue Edward VII, Henan Road, North Sichuan Road, and others often have public buses and trams running side by side. This greatly endangers traffic management, pedestrian safety, and the business of shops. Is it because the owner of the public bus company is the Chairman of the Municipal Council that they get this special convenience? The Municipal Council's reduction of rickshaws is based on the proposal of a few Western taxpayers. As representatives of more than one million Chinese taxpayers, we cannot sit idly by. For the sake of the needs of citizens and convenient transportation, we should restrict the routes of public buses and maintain the existing number of rickshaws. Otherwise, we will seek other effective ways to benefit the citizens and maintain traffic. We respectfully declare this and hope that you will understand."

Central Mint Review Committee Meeting; Approves the Number of Subsidiary Coins Minted in the Past Three Months

The Central Mint Review Committee held its 35th regular meeting at the Central Bank at 4:30 p.m. on the 11th of this month. The committee members present were Chen Jian'an, Li Shaoshi, Cui Jingyi, Ye Fuxiao, Chen Guangfu, Song Hanzhang, Mai Lai, Lu Xian, Xu Mike, Geng Aider, Lai Aisi, Dai Jingfu, Wu Yunqi, Hu Bijian, Sato, Yoshida Seiji, Rayne, Ye Zhuotang, Xu Xinliu, Lin Shu, Xide Mao, Qin Run, Shao Suishan, and others, twenty-three people in total. Wei Jingzhou, Deputy Director of the Central Mint, and Shi Daosheng, Secretary of the Committee, Ge Laide, Chemical Assayer, were present as nonvoting attendees. Kong Yongzhi, Chairman (who was unable to attend due to other matters and was replaced by Committee Member Chen An'an) presided over the meeting. Li Zhechang recorded the minutes. In addition to approving the minutes of the previous meeting, the secretary reported on the monitoring and sealing of Class B (880 fineness) mint bars for the months of June, July, and August of the 25th year of the Republic, totaling 108 bars in June, 379 bars in July, and 402 bars in August. In addition, the monitoring and sealing of five types of subsidiary coins were reported, totaling 2.74 million 20-cent nickel coins, 4.72 million 10-cent copper-nickel coins, 18.44 million 5-cent nickel coins, 23.38 million 1-cent copper coins, and 3.12 million half-cent copper coins in June; 5.68 million 20-cent nickel coins, 12.16 million 10-cent copper-nickel coins, 7.40 million 5-cent copper-nickel coins, 24.54 million 1-cent copper coins, and 720,000 half-cent copper coins in July; 9.57 million 20-cent nickel coins, 11.18 million 10-cent nickel coins, 1.16 million 5-cent nickel coins, 25.06 million 1-cent copper coins, and 960,000 half-cent copper coins in August. All were approved for release from the factory and were announced in a list. The examination of factory affairs, review of factory accounts, chemical assay of miscellaneous incoming bars, and the committee's work in June, July, and August were also reported in detail and approved by the regular meeting. The meeting adjourned at 5:10 p.m.

Sino-British Aviation: Joint Transportation to be Realized; Shanghai-Guangdong Planes Can Land in Hong Kong; Station to be Established After Permit Arrives

After the China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC) establishes a station in Hong Kong, and has obtained British approval, after the station is established, airmail destined for Britain arriving in Hong Kong can be jointly transported to Britain by British Overseas Airways Corporation (BOAC). A reporter from the China Eastern News Agency made a special visit yesterday morning to record the following:

Landing in Hong Kong

From the beginning of the CNAC's Shanghai-Guangdong route, there were plans to land in Hong Kong. However, due to the lack of British approval, it has not been realized until now. Later, the Ministry of Transportation consulted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the British Ambassador to China for a long time. Now it has been approved by the British side.

Sino-British Joint Transportation

According to the company's manager, Mr. Dai Enji, yesterday morning, the British side has agreed to the company's planes landing in Hong Kong. However, the permit from the Hong Kong authorities has not yet been delivered. Now, after the Hong Kong side's permit arrives, the preparations for establishing a station can be carried out, as well as contacting the post office and BOAC. As for Sino-British joint transportation, because there is already a BOAC regular air route from Hong Kong to (Berang) (near Singapore), flying once a week, in the future, mail destined for Britain, after being transported to Hong Kong by CNAC, can be transported to Britain by BOAC planes.

Establishing a Station in Macau

As for the station on the American Pacific air route closest to China, United Airlines has determined it to be Macau, and has obtained permission from the Portuguese government. However, it has not yet officially started flying. It is heard that Mr. Bixby is now in Macau. Furthermore, United Airlines also plans to establish a station in Hong Kong. Negotiations are being conducted in New York, but nothing has been heard here.

Head of Daishan Salt Fields Requests Withdrawal of Stationed Police

Since the tax police and fishermen dispute occurred in the Daishan Salt Fields in Liangzhe, Yu Bingdong, the former Deputy Director of the Liangzhe Salt Affairs Tax Police Bureau, concurrently Director of the Daishan Weighing and Distribution Bureau, and concurrently head of the salt fields, has been transferred back to his original position. The vacancy was filled by Mr. Zhu Xufan, the head of the Xiasu branch specially transferred from the Audit General Office. It is learned that Mr. Zhu arrived in Daishan on September 5th to take office. Mr. Zhu has been in politics for many years and is deeply aware of the people's needs. He is also forthright and capable. Upon arriving in Daishan, he immediately started handling all the follow-up matters, which has won general sympathy. It is also learned that Mr. Zhu, considering that the current situation has been resolved, specially submitted a request to his superiors the other day to withdraw all the patrol and independent battalion local police stationed in Daishan in order to reassure the people. Upon hearing the news, fishermen and salt workers in various districts have also returned one after another, and the original situation is gradually being restored.

The Entire City's Labor Circles Host Banquet for Pan Gongzhan; Chairman Hopes Government Will Support Labor; Director Pan and Guests Give Speeches

The Shanghai General Labor Union and all the city's labor unions held a banquet for Director of the Social Affairs Bureau Pan Gongzhan at the Atlantic Restaurant on Fuzhou Road at 7:00 PM on the 13th of this month. The details are recorded as follows:

Participating Guests and Hosts

Pan Gongzhan, Wu Kaixian, Lu Jingshi, Jiang Huaisuo, Mi Jifang, Xu Yefu, Wang Manyun, Lin Meiyan, Wu Hengru, Chen Junyi, Zhu Xuefan, Zhou Juxiang, Shao Xubai, Ye Xianggao, Long Yuting, Long Peiyun, Fan Yifeng, Shui Xiangyun, Li Mengnan, Lu Muqin, Hu Menglin, Yu Yaoqiu, Shi Jikuan, Li Hua, Liu Jintai, Ding Changyan, Shen Jiabin, Zhou Guangrong, Cao Zhimin, Bao Boyi, Zhang Dehua, as well as representatives from the cigarette rolling unions of the four districts, the water and electricity union of the first district, the match union of the fifth district, the postal service union, the postal worker union, the dried goods union, the rice cart union, the silk reeling union of the sixth district, the cotton spinning union of the tenth district, the military uniform union, the newspaper delivery union, the civilian ship union of the fourth district, the cosmetics union of the first district, the soap and pharmaceutical union of the ninth district, the candle industry union, the cleaning union of the first district, the tea making union of the sixth district, the sauce industry union, the hat making union of the fourth district, the cotton spinning union of the third district, the elevator driver union, the pharmaceutical union, the cotton spinning union of the fifth district, the towing and lightering union, the dyeing industry union, etc., more than one hundred people from over sixty labor unions attended.

Mr. Zhu's Speech

After several rounds of drinks, Zhu Xuefan, chairman of the General Labor Union, stood up to give a speech, which roughly stated: "Today, the labor circles of the entire city are hosting a banquet for Mr. Pan Gongzhan, director of the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau, and have invited leaders of the party and government organs to accompany us. We are deeply honored and grateful for your willingness to come. On behalf of the labor circles, I would like to express my deep gratitude. Director Pan is a pillar of the party and the country, and his morality, writing, behavior, and character have long been admired by us. When Director Pan was in charge of the Shanghai Agricultural, Commercial, and Labor Bureau and the Social Affairs Bureau in 1927, he achieved many successes in labor welfare and protection, from which the workers benefited greatly. After Mr. Wu Xingya's death, the central authorities still appointed Mr. Pan to succeed as Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, which is not only a lucky star for our labor circles but also a blessing for all the citizens of Shanghai. The situation of labor in Shanghai is more depressed than before, and the workers themselves feel deeply pained. Shanghai workers should have a turning point during this period. Now that Mr. Pan has succeeded as Director of the Social Affairs Bureau, I hope that he will provide more development and assistance to our labor in the future. On behalf of the comrades in the labor circles of the entire city, I have prepared a meager feast to wish Director Pan a boundless future in social undertakings."

Mr. Pan's Speech

After the chairman's speech, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau Pan Gongzhan stood up and gave a speech, saying, "Gentlemen, leaders of the labor circles, I will sincerely accept what the chairman said. I hope that in the future, we can reach a broad and bright path step by step through difficulties. As the person in charge of the Social Affairs Bureau, my first certainty is that the labor circles of the entire city will help the government and cooperate fully. The second certainty is that we will follow the norms of the former Director Wu and solve all difficulties gradually. However, I still feel like I am facing a deep abyss and treading on thin ice with fear and trepidation. Now the country has entered an extraordinary period, and the future of the entire country and the entire nation is dangerous and uncertain. Recently, the internal unity of the party and the atmosphere of peace are spreading, and there is a new atmosphere of carrying on the past and opening up the future, which seems optimistic. But looking around, the enemy is watching and has ambitions to destroy our country and nation at any time. The Shanghai market environment is on the eve of extreme danger. All sectors of agriculture, industry, commerce, and education should temporarily put aside their own interests and prioritize the country and the nation, obey the central government, support the leader, and take unified steps to cope with the difficulties and absolutely avoid creating an unmanageable situation between classes. I hope that the leaders of all labor unions will always enlighten all workers to concentrate on organization, unify action, open up the difficulties of the country and the nation, and seek the great path of permanent survival." Afterwards, guests Xu Yefu, Shao Xubai, a member of the Standing Committee of the General Labor Union, and Liu Jintai, a representative of the labor union, gave speeches one after another. Drinks were exchanged, and the guests and hosts dispersed in joy at about 9:00 PM.

Abundant National Cotton Harvest Confirmed; Cotton Mills Starting Up; High Cotton Prices and Low Yarn Prices Will Change; Restoring the Original Market Situation of the Past

After the estimated abundant harvest of domestic cotton is gradually confirmed, the situation of the cotton industry has improved somewhat. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency made a special trip to interview people in the cotton industry to inquire about the current and future situation of the cotton industry, as follows: There are many reasons for the depression of China's cotton industry in the past. The main reason was high cotton prices and low yarn prices. The reason for high cotton prices was the shortage of domestic cotton. The reason for low yarn prices was the poor situation in rural areas and the sluggish market for yarn and cloth. This situation is now gradually improving.

Domestic Cotton

This year is very good. The previous report from the Cotton Industry Statistics Conference reported that the output could reach 16 million dan. Recently, the Japanese cotton merchant Toyo Cotton Line also reported 14-15 million dan. It seems that it can always be calculated at over 14 million dan, which is more than enough to meet the demand. In the future, the price of cotton will not be more expensive than cotton yarn, which can be determined. As for the cotton yarn and cloth market, since the yarn factories have successively reduced production and stopped production last year, the output has been greatly reduced. In the past three or four months, the cotton yarn and cloth market has been very good, so the inventory of cotton yarn and cloth has decreased day by day. According to a recent survey, the current remaining cotton yarn in Shanghai is a total of more than 58,000 bales, which is more than 14,000 bales less than a month ago, and the decrease in Chinese factories is

The Most, a Decrease

Of more than 11,000 bales, which is due to the good sales of yarn in August. Now, the yarn produced by the Chinese yarn factories in Shanghai totals 54,000 bales, of which 28,000 bales are in the warehouses of the Yarn and Cloth Exchange, and only 16,000 bales are in the yarn factories, which is a very small number. In the past few days, the sales of yarn and cloth have been very good, and the yarn factories have sold a lot of futures for October, November, and December, so the number of yarn and cloth in stock will not increase in the next three or four months. This year, the agricultural products of various provinces have generally had bumper harvests, and there are not many areas of famine, so the sales of yarn and cloth have improved considerably. When new cotton comes on the market in the future, yarn factories

Will Gradually Start Work, and They Will Be Able to Sell Their Products Without Fear of Accumulation. It is not difficult to change from cheap yarn and expensive cotton to expensive yarn and cheap cotton. The time for the change is when the new cotton is successively put on the market. Recently, there has been a gradual trend in this direction. The prices quoted by the exchange show that cotton yarn is high in the near term and low in the long term, while cotton is low in the near term and high in the long term, which is clear evidence. However, the meaning of expensive yarn and cheap cotton is only in relation to the cheap yarn and expensive cotton of the past. It does not mean that cotton prices will fall alone or yarn prices will rise alone. Rather, yarn will rise more than cotton when they rise together, and yarn will fall less than cotton when they fall together. This direction is to restore the original market situation of the past and to bring the economic status of yarn and cotton above normal. As a result, yarn factories have become active, and many of the factories that have stopped work are preparing to start work.

Shanghai

Hengfeng has decided to start work and is now reorganizing. Shenxin Two Five and Zhenhua are also planning. The Zhensheng of Hankou has been taken over by the Changzhou Dacheng Yarn Factory. Hankou First is jointly operated by Hankou merchants and the Jiujiang Lizhong Yarn Factory. However, Minsheng has not yet made a decision because the machinery is relatively old. The Saicheng, Yuyuan, and Beiyang of Tianjin, which have stopped work, have also been bought by the Japanese and are rushing to reorganize and start the machines. At present, there are still 800,000 spindles in yarn factories that have stopped work. If all of them start work, they can use a lot more cotton, reducing the surplus of the bumper cotton harvest. In the future, expensive yarn and cheap cotton is expected to change slowly. Otherwise, the change will be as sudden as it was in 1924.

Opinions of the Banking and Finance Industries on the Levy of Income Tax; Foreign Merchants Should Implement It Simultaneously to Avoid Capital Flight; Procedures are Insufficiently Prepared, Requesting Postponement; Decision to Send Representatives to Visit Relevant Officials to State Their Case

After the Ministry of Finance established the Central Direct Tax Preparatory Office to handle the collection of income tax, the income tax of the second category "income from bonds and savings, that is, income from public bonds, company bonds, stocks, and interest on savings," was set at 5%, and the collection was set for October 1st. The Executive Committee of the Money Industry Association resolved to copy the income tax regulations and send them to all member money shops for study. If there are any opinions, please submit them to the association within one week for collection and handling. The Banking Association held an Executive Committee meeting at 2:00 PM on the 12th, and resolved to appoint three representatives to visit the officials in charge of income tax collection to state their opinions. Furthermore, a reporter from the New Voice News Agency inquired from the banking and finance industries yesterday. The details are described separately as follows:

Banking Sector

(1) Banks handle final accounts at the end of June and the end of December each year. Interest on various savings is settled at the time of the final accounts. Now that the income tax on savings interest is implemented on October 1st, the banks will inevitably have to handle the final accounts again at the end of September. Now that time is approaching, the procedures are insufficiently prepared, so it is hoped that the government will implement the income tax on savings interest on January 1st of next year at the same time as other taxes. The petition to the Ministry of Finance to review and seize the postponement of the event is currently being drafted and will be submitted in the next day or two. (2) For the income tax on interest on interbank savings, for example, if Bank A deposits a certain amount of money in Bank B, and Bank B deposits a certain amount of money in Bank A at the same time, it is requested that the income tax on the interest be handled in a flexible manner. (3) Foreign banks should simultaneously implement the collection of income tax on interest on savings, otherwise, there will inevitably be a risk of capital flight from Chinese banks. Please pay attention to this. Therefore, representatives will be sent to visit Gao Bingfang, the Director of the Central Direct Tax Preparatory Office, and Liang Hejun, the Deputy Director, to state their opinions and request adoption.

Finance Sector

Expressed agreement in principle with the collection of income tax on interest on savings and hopes that foreign banks will implement it simultaneously to avoid capital flight. However, how to collect it is considered to be in need of research, so letters are sent to various money shops to solicit opinions. It is decided that after the opinions of various money shops are collected, a meeting will be held to discuss them collectively. However, there is a deep fear that the implementation on October 1st will not be sufficiently prepared.

Ship Losses

Dongchuan Collides with Xuzhou

The Xuzhou, a ship of the China United Shipping Company of this port, has a deadweight of 1,658.15 tons, a registered tonnage of 926 tons, can load 2,400 tons of cargo, is 253.5 feet long, 35.9 feet wide, 17.8 feet deep, and has a draft of 16.6 feet. The ship currently sails on the Shanghai-Haizhou-Lianyungang route. This time, the ship went to Laoyao, Haizhou, to load coal. Yesterday, the shipowner sent an urgent telegram to Shanghai reporting that the Xuzhou was violently collided with by the large iron barge Dongchuan of Kangzhenji. The Xuzhou was unable to avoid it, resulting in the iron plates on the port side of the stern being completely broken, and a large hole was immediately created. The losses were enormous. The telegram was brief and the details are unknown. After receiving the report, the United Company, in addition to notifying the insurance company, urgently telegraphed Haizhou, ordering the Xuzhou shipowner to quickly report the cause of the collision in detail as soon as possible, so that a protest could be lodged.

Shihe Drops Anchor

The Shihe, a ship of the Gongji Shipping Company, has a capacity of 2,100 tons, a gross tonnage of 1,513 tons, a length of 232.2 feet, and a draft of 17.6 feet. The ship is currently transporting coal on the Yangtze River. Yesterday, Gongji received a report from the Shihe shipowner that the large iron anchor on the starboard side of the Shihe was suddenly lost and sank to the bottom of the river when the Shihe set sail from Hankou at 12:00 PM on the 12th. The loss was enormous. In addition to trying to salvage it, the company was telegraphed to quickly send a new anchor for use.

Economic Commission Announces Prices of Autumn Cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang; Production Volume Approximately 380,000 Dan; Manufacturers Depart to Purchase

The autumn cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces will soon be on the market, and silk cocoon manufacturers have begun to depart to purchase them. The National Economic Commission has officially announced the standard prices for southern cocoons. The total output of autumn cocoons in the two provinces this year is 380,000 dan (market weight). The details are recorded as follows:

Announced Prices

The Silk Improvement Committee of the National Economic Commission officially announced the standard prices for autumn cocoons: "It is hereby announced that the committee's ninth executive meeting discussed the issue of the standard prices for autumn cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang this term. After deliberation, it was decided that the price of raw silk per dan for the current autumn cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang shall be set at 670 yuan in national currency, based on the average price of New York and Yokohama futures and spot prices. In addition, the wages for reeling are set at 80 yuan per dan, and the expenses for collecting and drying cocoons are set at 26 yuan. The cocoon ratio is 290 catties. The cocoon price is calculated according to the size of the cocoon ratio. For example, if the cocoon ratio is 460 catties, the price of fresh cocoons is 29 yuan per market dan. If the cocoon ratio is 430 catties, the cocoon price is 32 yuan. If the cocoon ratio is 500 catties, the cocoon price is 26 yuan," etc. This is hereby announced for general knowledge.

Deadline for Payment of Security Deposit

The Zhejiang Provincial Silk Cocoon Control Committee issued an announcement to approve the amount of cocoon purchases by each merchant and set a deadline for the payment of security deposits: "It is hereby announced that the committee has handled the registration of silk cocoon merchants and the purchase of autumn cocoons in this province and has been closed on schedule. After review and determination, in addition to separately ordering and notifying the original registered merchants, the list of security deposits approved for each cocoon purchasing store is hereby publicly announced. The merchants concerned are requested to pay the above-mentioned security deposits in full at the Bank of China from now until the 17th of this month, obtain the bank's deposit receipt, and then go to the committee to exchange for a formal receipt. Do not delay. This is hereby announced." The approved manufacturers include (1) 18 silk factories in this province, such as Qingyun, (2) 39 silk factories from other provinces, such as Meifeng, and (3) 7 cocoon merchants, such as Baochang. However, the Qiaosi Cooperative, Zhuji Yongning Cooperative, and Haining Wangmiao Cooperative are exempt from paying security deposits.

Manufacturers Purchase

Fresh autumn cocoons will soon be on the market. The production volume in Jiangsu is 200,000 dan, and the production volume in Zhejiang is 180,000 dan (market weight). The price of autumn cocoons has been set by the Silk Improvement Committee of the National Economic Commission, with reeling as the standard. The price is from 32 yuan to 26 yuan per dan, with 25 yuan as the central price. All cocoon firms have prepared to weigh them. Silk cocoon manufacturers in Shanghai, Wuxi, Hangzhou, and other places have registered with the Zhejiang Provincial Silk Control Committee and have now begun to pay security deposits to the Bank of China designated by the committee. The security deposit for each double stove is 100 yuan. After obtaining the bank's temporary receipt and returning to the committee to exchange for a formal receipt, they can go to the production area to collect cocoons. The deadline for paying the security deposit is set for the 17th of this month. If it is not paid by the deadline, the registration will be canceled. Therefore, all manufacturers are now paying the security deposit in full according to the registered amount of cocoons. Some silk cocoon manufacturers have seen new autumn cocoons on the market and have successfully borrowed money from the banking industry. In order to prepare as soon as possible, they have sent personnel to work with the bank representatives who borrowed the money to depart to purchase cocoons.

New Cotton from Various Places Appears on the Market; First Batch of Nantong Cotton Arrives in Shanghai, Market Price Expected to Exceed 45 Yuan; Japanese Merchants Profit Greatly from Buying New Cotton

According to a Shen Shi News Agency report, new cotton from various places has now appeared on the market successively. Except for a few areas where the harvest was poor due to the autumn rains, most areas reported abundant harvests. It is reported that the earliest new cotton from Yuyao, which has arrived in Shanghai, has reached about 17,000 bales. The first batch of new cotton from counties such as Nantong in northern Jiangsu also arrived in Shanghai yesterday, totaling more than 20,000 bales. However, cotton purchased by various yarn factories in the producing areas has not yet been shipped to Shanghai. As for the price of new cotton, it is higher than that of old cotton due to the estimated reduction in U.S. cotton production, the soaring price of yarn, and the strong demand in various places. Market participants predict that the top-quality new cotton in the future may exceed 45 yuan per picul. As a result, transactions have been quite active recently, a situation not seen when new cotton entered the market in previous years. It is also reported that this year, Japanese merchants are buying new Chinese cotton by sending personnel to various places in advance to order futures, that is, setting prices and paying for orders in advance, and delivering goods in full when they enter the market, so they have made a lot of profit. Moreover, in addition to supplying their own factories, they also sell the spot cotton they collect to customers, so China has lost a lot from their transactions.

Heavy Fog in the City Yesterday Morning; The Whole City Was Dark, Like Early Evening; A Sudden High Tide in the Huangpu River Last Night

According to a Datong News Agency report, after the weather cleared up in this port, there was heavy fog again yesterday morning, and the darkness was like early evening. The tide in the Huangpu River was quite high in the afternoon. The details of each situation are recorded as follows:

Heavy Fog

The continuous autumn rains in this port made people feel quite uncomfortable. The sky began to clear up the afternoon before yesterday, and the weather became clear. However, yesterday at dawn, heavy fog suddenly arose, and the whole city was dark, like early evening. It did not dissipate until after 9:00 a.m. During the foggy period, shops opened and operated with electric lights, and streetcars moved slowly.

High Tide Last Night

The Huangpu River has been experiencing high tides for several days due to the autumn flood season. According to the Huangpu River Dredging Bureau's forecast, the tide that occurred at 11:42 p.m. last night was quite large, with a predicted amount of 12 feet, 2.5 inches, less than one foot from the Bund embankment, so it deserves special attention. The tide started to rise after 9:00 p.m. last night. By 11:15 p.m., the tide was rising rapidly, and the water flow rate was approximately 2.0 nautical miles per hour. It began to recede at 2:20 a.m. today.

The Shanghai Merchant Steam Navigation Company's Various Wharves Complete Labor Tendering; Saving More Than 110,000 Yuan Annually

The Shanghai Merchant Steam Navigation Company's expenses are the highest for labor, reaching hundreds of thousands of yuan per year. This labor has always been handled by people who are not recruited by the bureau, so the rate is relatively high, and the leakage is more than tens of thousands of yuan every year. Therefore, since the reorganization of the bureau, the Ministry of Communications has attached great importance to labor expenses, and before starting to reorganize wharf affairs, it first reformed the labor item. It previously drafted rules and regulations and openly invited bids, which were handled by the bureau. After the advertisement was published in the newspaper, people from all parties who requested to bid to the bureau were very enthusiastic. It is now heard that the tendering of labor for the North, Central, South, New, and Hua wharves of the bureau has been completed. The completion of the bureau's labor tendering is the basic work for reorganizing wharf operations, and the significant reduction in labor expenses is undoubtedly the initial success in saving wharf expenses. According to the bureau's recent calculation, the labor expenditure of each wharf in the 24th year of the Republic was 205,846.53 yuan for the South Wharf, 26,182.62 yuan for the New Wharf, 53,754.36 yuan for the North Wharf, 39,265.61 yuan for the Central Wharf, and 10,108.57 yuan for the Hua Wharf, totaling 335,157.69 yuan. Now, the tendering results show that the labor rate has been reduced to 63.5% for the South Wharf, 50.5% for the New Wharf, 74.5% for the North Wharf, 74% for the Central Wharf, and 73% for the Hua Wharf. According to this rate, if the labor expenditure in the 24th year of the Republic is used as the standard for calculation, the South Wharf can save 75,133.98 yuan, the New Wharf can save 12,960.40 yuan, the North Wharf can save 13,707.36 yuan, the Central Wharf can save 10,209.06 yuan, and the Hua Wharf can save 2,729.31 yuan, totaling 114,740.11 yuan for the five wharves. This figure is only based on the bureau's business situation in the 24th year of the Republic. If the bureau's wharf business develops and cargo transportation increases in the future, the expenses saved will be more than this number. The bureau's reorganization keynotes are nothing more than increasing revenue and reducing expenditure. The revenue increase should start with the development of business, which has gradually shown a thriving trend. As for reducing expenditure, the effect of the labor tendering is the most significant.

Xing Zhigang Requests to Build a Nanhuiguan Wharf

Xing Zhigang, a representative of the western shipping industry in Pudong, yesterday presented a petition to the Shanghai Municipal Government requesting the construction of a public wharf at Nanhuiguan, requesting that orders be given to the Engineering and Public Works Bureaus to plan and proceed with the construction in order to promote commerce. The petition stated, "Looking south from the Bund outside the Sixteenth Shop to the Dongjiadu Wharf, the wheel ports are densely packed and the warehouses are towering. The original wharves for civilian ships transporting goods from various ports have all been demolished and rented out as wheel port shorelines for profit. Therefore, civilian ships are crowded, and the one or two public wharves are difficult to dock. As a result, the goods of various merchants along the streets inside and outside the Nanshi area are difficult to load and unload, transportation is hindered, and commerce is scattered, which has a significant impact on the market. It is not a trivial matter... The Nanhuiguan Wharf is convenient for transportation. It is a gathering place for ships from various townships in Southern, Sichuan, and other counties... Since the Public Works and Engineering Bureaus considered this and set up a magnetic card to designate it as a public wharf, the wharf has not yet been built. Moreover, since the wharves for civilian ships at each port were merged, there are more and more ships coming, and if a public wharf is not rebuilt, merchants from the four townships will have no way to disembark, and transportation will be hindered. Those who have not been there in person cannot understand the suffering. The Shanghai Huangpu River Dredging Bureau has considered this and has repeatedly sent machine ships to dredge the area around the wharf for several days to avoid the shallow obstruction of ships. Now, because the wharf is narrow and blocked by wood rows, ships from the four townships still cannot dock and are in a desperate situation. Therefore, I venture to appeal to your honor to consider that the wharf is the lifeline of transportation, and transportation is the center of commerce. Please order the Public Works and Public Utilities Bureaus to build a public wharf at Nanhuiguan, according to the plan of the former Jian Gongyi Public Wharf, in order to benefit航旅 and engage in commerce, and I will be very grateful."

The Sino-Japanese Joint Trademark Compilation Is Published

The Trademark Compilation, which was started by the Trademark Bureau of the Ministry of Industry when the former director was in office, took three years to complete. It was entrusted by the bureau to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to be printed by the Zhonghua Book Company and is now published. Its content is divided into two major compilations: the Chinese section and the Japanese section. The book is 5 inches high, 6 inches wide, and 11 inches long, with a total of more than 2,500 pages. It is printed in fine detail on Daolin paper. All the trademarks used by industries and businesses in China and Japan are collected without omission. There are also more than 100 inscriptions by important figures from the National Government in the front of the book, which are undoubtedly valuable. It is truly an essential treasure for national industry and commerce associations, libraries, lawyers, accountants, and commercial artists. The actual price of the book is 15 yuan, and it is exclusively sold by the Stationery Department on the second floor of the Guohuo Shopping Mall of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. In order to popularize it, the association is temporarily selling it at half price, limited to 1,000 copies, and will not be lenient beyond the deadline.

Economic Statistics Research Institute Completes Two Major Projects: Shanghai's Development and Industry, and Overview of Wuxing Farmers' Economy

The China Economic Statistics Research Institute is jointly established by the Chinese Economic Society and the Chinese Statistical Society, and is presided over by Liu Da-jun, He Lian, He De-kui, Li Zhao-huan, Sheng Jun, and ten other committee members. The institute aims to study China's economic problems using statistical methods. Since its establishment, it has conducted numerous surveys and studies. The recent completed works of the institute include: (1) comprehensively studying the institute's past surveys on Shanghai's industry and the impact of industry on urban socio-economics, and compiling a book in English titled "Shanghai's Development and Industry," which is the research report for the Pacific Conference held in the United States this year. The Chinese version will be published by the Sun Yat-sen Culture and Education Center in the future. The book's first chapter is an introduction, the second chapter is the evolution of Shanghai's industrial development, the third chapter is recent development, the fourth chapter is the characteristics of Shanghai's industry, the fifth chapter is Shanghai's labor, the sixth chapter is the economic impact of Shanghai's industrialization, the seventh chapter is the social impact of Shanghai's industrialization, and the eighth chapter is the conclusion. It also includes seven statistical tables and explanations of past surveys conducted in 1928, 1929, 1931, 1933, and 1934, totaling over 280 pages, with a total of 473 pages. It is a hardback volume selling for ten yuan. It is available at the Commercial Press and Beteridge & Co. (2) In the spring of 1935, the institute investigated the economic conditions of the silk-producing areas of Nanxun, Linghu, Shuanglin, and Yuanjiawei towns in Wuxing (Huzhou), Zhejiang. One form was filled out for each farming household. By the end of May last year, more than 1,000 survey forms had been filled out. However, some forms were deemed unsatisfactory and were eliminated. A total of 420 forms were adopted and analyzed. The statistical work and report preparation began in June last year and are now mostly completed. The "Overview of Farmers' Household Economy in Wuxing" was first published in the third volume, seventh issue of the institute's "Economic Statistics Monthly." Each issue of the magazine costs two jiao. Shanghai Magazine Company and Dagongbao Agency Department both sell it. Those who wish to subscribe can contact the institute at 88 Zhao Bishop Road, Shanghai. The annual subscription fee is two yuan, postage included.

National Labor Bureau Statistics, Total Number of Laborers in the Country, Totaling More Than 110 Million People, Without Unemployment, It Would Not Exceed

According to the survey conducted by the National Labor Bureau, the number of male and female workers in China's industry, handicrafts (including occupations), miners, transportation workers (including aviation, railway, postal and telecommunications workers, and rickshaw pullers), and hired farmers (workers hired by small farmers), totals more than 110 million people, including unemployed workers. This accounts for more than a quarter of the total population of the country. If there is no unemployment panic and everyone can make the most of their talents, China would not be a backward producer and become an import-surplus country. Now, Cheng Haifeng, the director of the National Labor Bureau, has compiled an investigation report on the domestic labor situation and submitted it to the central competent authority for reference, so as to seek a comprehensive relief plan.

She had abdominal pain a few days ago, and the amniotic fluid was broken by the midwife, but the fetus still did not descend. Ms. Duizhen was also invited to go, and she used forceps to perform surgery, and it was safely delivered. Both mother and child are safe.

Zhang Guanghua Dies for Love by Jumping into River from Ferry – Han Village Owner Values Money Over Morality, Detains Courtesan in Attempt to Sell Her

Zhang Guanghua, from Haining, 32 years old, worked in the stock exchange and was unmarried. This spring, he frequented the Han Village opened by Xu Axing at 142 Ailaige Road in the French Concession, where he met the prostitute Feng Qingying. They fell in love with each other and wished to be together forever. He discussed the matter with the village owner, and Zhang prepared 80 yuan to redeem Feng. After they lived together, Zhang's income was very meager and insufficient to cover the living expenses of the two, so Feng continued to stay in the village, selling herself and sharing the proceeds. Later, in April, it was heard that another girl in the village was being redeemed. Shan Feng acted as a guarantor for the transaction. The matter was discovered by the French Concession police, who considered buying and selling people as illegal. All those involved were arrested and investigated, and the case was closed. The village owner claimed to have spent 1,000 yuan on expenses, which should be borne by the buyer, seller, and guarantor. As a result, Feng was forced to pay 300 yuan, but she was unable to deliver it. Therefore, Zhang Guanghua wrote a promissory note for 300 yuan for the village owner to hold, and monthly interest had to be added. Unexpectedly, the village owner, Xu A, saw that it would be difficult to get the money back soon, and another client had taken a fancy to Feng, willing to pay a large sum to buy Feng as his wife. Seeing that the opportunity had arrived, the village owner first pressured Zhang and Feng to repay the loan (i.e., the 300 yuan), but they could not. Then, Feng was detained, and she was forced to be sold. Zhang had redeemed her first, and the two were deeply in love, and Zhang could not bear to let her be taken away. He could not get Feng back, and, in extreme anger, became tired of life. At 8:00 PM the night before last, he boarded the Chunbei Line No. 16 city ferry at the Bund on Beijing Road to Pugu. When the ferry arrived at the Chunjiang Wharf, Zhang did not disembark but stayed on the boat to return to Puxi. The sailors did not pay attention to this strange passenger. When the ferry returned to the Beijing Road Wharf, Zhang suddenly jumped into the river to kill himself. Fortunately, he was rescued by the sailors and sent to the Maritime Customs Police Station. After hearing the whole story, the police chief ordered him to be sent to the local court for questioning the Han Village owner.

Spring and Autumn Annals

Snippets

– (Zhang Huang)

Even with mature teeth and holding a high position, one still feels immature, as if it were not long ago that one was playing around one's parents' knees. Having a good family, the words and deeds of one's own family, formerly treated with utmost reverence, gradually become annoying, and even one's own body is considered a superfluous burden.

A new daughter-in-law is not happy with her mother-in-law or with her husband’s younger siblings, because she is considered an outsider. The mother-in-law starts it, and the younger siblings follow suit, making things worse. The old father usually acts deaf and dumb because the money for marrying the daughter-in-law came from him, and he endures it for the sake of his money.

Parents invariably wish their children to be successful. If one son is unwilling, they urge his brothers to help, hoping that he will change. Spreading love leads to excessive expectations. Sisters-in-law and brothers-in-law argue reasonably, gradually becoming incompatible. Thus, peers become antagonistic, greatly hurting their parents' feelings!

A Record of Revolutionary Elder Mr. You Lie

– Qian Da

Mr. You Lie, who recently came to Shanghai, is truly a revolutionary elder. In the late Qing Dynasty, he was as famous as Sun Yat-sen, Chen Shaobai, and Yang Heling, known as the Four Heroes. He was one of the earliest founders of the Revive China Society. Later, when the society was reorganized into the Tongmenghui (United League), he led the alliance in the Nanyang region. Countless overseas Chinese were inspired by him to engage in revolution. The name "Republic of China" was determined by Mr. You Lie and Sun Yat-sen in Japan. After the Wuchang Uprising, Mr. You rushed to Yunnan to urge the southwestern provinces to revolt, and the whole country followed. After the establishment of the Republic of China, Yuan Shikai tried to appease him with titles and honors, but Mr. You was unmoved. Instead, he organized the National Salvation Army to denounce Yuan's crimes. After Yuan's downfall, Mr. You retired to Hong Kong. In 1921, when Sun Yat-sen established his government in Guangzhou and took office as the Extraordinary President, he repeatedly sent envoys to invite Mr. You, but Mr. You firmly declined. Now, due to his advanced age, Hong Kong is not suitable for recuperation, and Speaker Sun of the Legislative Yuan happened to telegraph him to visit the north. Therefore, he took a boat to Shanghai with great interest, rested for a while, and will then travel to various places to enjoy himself. Mr. You is currently residing at No. 15 Jisi Fei Road, the residence of Mr. Tan Haiqiu. With the introduction of Mr. Tan and Mr. You's secretary, Ma Baimei, I once visited Mr. You at Qiupu. Mr. You said that he had suffered from storms on the journey and had not yet recovered his energy, so we did not talk much. Mr. Ma Baimei showed me a photo of five young men in their twenties. I have forgotten the surname of one of them, but the other four were Mr. You, Sun Yat-sen, Chen Shaobai, and Yang Heling. The photo was taken in 1888, more than thirty years ago. In these decades, how many changes have taken place in the world! And all of Mr. You's old friends from those years are now buried in the ground. I know that if Mr. You caresses this photo, he will surely feel a sense of沧桑(cāngsāng, vicissitudes).

Yang the Comprador

– Hua Ling

Yang the Comprador is the landlord of our lane. Because he used to work as a comprador in a foreign firm for more than 30 years, he is now retired and lives off the rent of more than 50 shikumen (stone-gated) houses in the lane, as well as some stock dividends. But everyone still calls him Yang the Comprador.

Yang the Comprador is already over 70 years old, but his desire for women is still as strong as when he was young. He lives in a specially built three-story house. The upstairs is occupied by his first wife, sons, daughters-in-law, and grandchildren, while the downstairs is occupied by his second wife, a once-famous courtesan, and a middle school student who has not graduated from a certain girls' school.

Two years ago, Yang the Comprador had an affair with a relatively unknown actress in a song and dance troupe and rented a house outside to keep her hidden. Last year, he met a radio announcer and got involved with her too. This year, he simply indulged in his old passions and frequented dance halls. He frequented dance halls, but he didn't dance. He knew that he was too old and weak to move around on the dance floor, so he always hired dance hostesses to sit with him. This won him the support of many dance hostesses, and finally, a 19-year-old dance hostess joined his group of stars.

Originally, he had one wife and two concubines. In the past three years, he has acquired three more, each living in a small villa outside, not connected to each other. This inevitably involved a lot of running around, and there was no one to take care of them. So recently, he evicted the tenants from the adjacent two-story house and moved the three new concubines together for convenience.

His friends, seeing him surrounded by such a large group of wives and concubines without any conflicts, admired his skillful methods and asked him for advice. He always laughed loudly, stroked his beard, and then replied in a methodical manner, "What's so rare about that? To be honest, they are like flowers, how could they love an old man like me? What they love is nothing but my banknotes. I give each of them what they want, and naturally all the other problems are easily solved."

According to him, "He has married one wife and fourteen concubines in his life. He can't even remember how many other informal relationships he has had. Most of his income in his life has been spent on this. Now that his income is decreasing, he doesn't dare to mess around so much."

Indeed, in recent years, it has been rumored that he has mortgaged the entire lane of houses.——But although his situation is not as good as before, he still marries a concubine every year.

The Mated Phoenix

– By Zhang Henshui

Chapter Six: The Stern Face Reveals Kind Words, the Parrot Hears Secrets – The Beautiful Eyebrows Hold Heroic Spirit, Asking about the Kunlun Pledge

Xiao Ju poured tea into the teacups on the table, not saying anything, just smiling. Menglan said, "Look at this girl, I don't know what valuable thing she has picked up that she keeps giggling about." Xiao Ju said, "Am I eavesdropping? I've been sitting by the railing for a long time. I only heard the two young ladies whispering and laughing, but I didn't hear what they were saying." She finished her explanation, put down the teapot, and walked out on her own. But she blocked the door, poked half of her head in, and looked at the two. And she looked at Youmei, pointed at Menglan several times with her index finger. Menglan laughed: "Go away, you little devil, what are you doing?" Xiao Ju flicked her tongue at them, and walked away. Youmei heard the sound of the stairs fading away, and said: "She's gone far away, you can tell me what you want to tell me now." Menglan stroked her chest, frowning and saying, "If I could tell you, I would have told you long ago, why would I need you to ask me again and again?" After saying this, she sighed softly. Youmei shook her hands and laughed: "I won't ask you anymore, I won't ask you anymore, don't get sick because of my questions." Menglan laughed. "Actually, I don't have the heart to talk to that one person specifically. You can send many words into my ears, but my heart will be paying attention to something else. So, whether I smile or sigh, the person sitting opposite me doesn't have to pay attention, my attitude has nothing to do with the person in front of me. I don't know why I'm like this. To say it in a trendy way, maybe I don't have a soul? Youmei, I'm very sorry, talking to a good friend like you, I don't listen properly. I'm afraid I've lost face in front of my old friend." Youmei laughed: "You don't have to apologize so much. Saying it like that, Miss, you are so pitiful. I can't help but shed a few tears with you!" Menglan said: "I don't want you to pity me. Wanting people to pity you is something that weak people do." Youmei laughed: "The more I talk to you in private, the more you complain. I won't say anything anymore, you rest well at home." As she spoke, she placed her hand on Menglan's shoulder and patted her lightly. Menglan said: "What's the matter? Are you leaving?" Youmei said: "I think you're distracted, you should rest well. If I'm here, you have to keep talking with me, which will tire your spirit." As she spoke, she took her hand, and walked towards the door. Menglan didn't try to keep her, she took her hand and led her to the doorway. Youmei walked down the stairs, and still showing half of her body, turned her head back and waved her hands at Menglan, Menglan smiled at her inexplicably, and did not say anything else. Youmei went downstairs, and Menglan, with some reluctance, stood leaning on the railing, looking down. Youmei stood in the courtyard, and sure enough, she turned her head back and laughed, "Don't be dazed, go to sleep properly." (74)

The Art of Preserving Youthful Looks

– Song Guobin

When friends ask me about the art of preserving youthful looks, I write this article to answer them. The text reads:

A guest asked me, "You are over forty years old, yet your complexion is rosy and full, your skin is full of blood, and you look like you are not even twenty. I am very puzzled! I have been your friend for twenty years! And you don't seem to age. If not, the black hair should be streaked with gray, and the smooth face should be wrinkled! Longevity and prolonged vision are the wild talks of immortals, and rejuvenating oneself is the innovation of scientific medicine. Therefore, there are beauty salons and ways to preserve youthful looks. You are a doctor, so do you have a so-called "secret art"? What is the technique? I hope you won't keep it a secret forever." I said, "Yes, yes, my technique is different from others. People's techniques seek to overcome nature with medicine and skills, while my technique is simply to follow nature. Confucius said, 'People are born upright, but bending them will result in good fortune and avoidance of calamity.' Birth, death, growth, and aging are the norm for people, but how many people in the world ignore the art of preserving life and distort their lives? When I was young, I was often sick, weak, and frail. The name of being thin was known to my relatives. Later, I studied in Shanghai, specializing in medicine, and gradually learned the way to preserve life. Therefore, my daily life, movement, and rest all have routines, and my diet and rest all have rules. For decades, I have remained the same. That is my first technique. I am naturally indifferent and forgetful about fame and fortune. I have no interest in officialdom and no desire for wealth. Although I do not have the lofty aspirations of Chu Kuang, I admire the meaning of Yan Hui's satisfaction and contentment. I consider self-sufficiency as wealth, desirelessness as nobility, tranquility as pleasure, and not being humiliated as honor. Therefore, I live in optimism throughout my life, and times of pessimism are always rare. That is my second technique. I have no addictions, only a love for reading. Sounds and sights are not for me, and I hate smoking and drinking. All habits that are harmful to the body are avoided. That is my third technique. Those who write and paint at night greatly damage their spirit, those who pursue fame and fortune laboriously endanger their lives, and those who indulge in sounds and sights cut down their nature with two axes. I secretly pity them. Therefore, the art of preserving youthful looks is to follow nature. My technique is neither strange nor unusual, just common sense. But people don't understand, and they want to use medicine and surgery to achieve the magical effect of immortality. Isn't that abandoning the fundamental and pursuing the superficial?" The guest heard my words, seemed to understand, nodded slightly, sighed, bowed again, and left.

Two More Poems Collected from Contemporary Talents

Mr. Chen Xiaodie sent a seven-character ancient poem from Japan, embedding the characters for this year (歲) and 元 (first) to participate in the International Hotel Spring Banquet, and using Mr. Chen's elegant name for harmony. It was published in this newspaper on August 25th. Now, knowing that the harmony poems of Mr. Xu Xiaochu and Mr. Zhou Bangshi of the new pharmaceutical industry have been completed, I will also follow the example of Mr. Chen Xiaodie, removing my own name and embedding the elegant names of other gentlemen, and I will record them below.

In the past, under the Jiao lonely tung tree, a Yaoqin song "Extend Pine" sounded, "Boyuan" sat as an old guest, and "Dachao" spoke of the fiery sky. The rooster reported that "Xiaochu" was silent, and the morning "Guangfu" shone through the window. With "Bangjun" a hero of both literature and martial arts, old "Gongzhan" could draw a six-stone bow. The young men were from good families, playing "Yuesheng" to attract phoenixes. Sailing together, "Jicheng" became sworn brothers, day by day engraving "Xinzhining" into the soup. With the beauty of "Yushu" as a maiden, who knows which is longer? The new folk friendship is thin as the clouds, and Miss "Xiaodie" comes with orchids and fragrance. The thread of "Yiping" is ten feet high, with "Shao Chuan" flowing into the sea. Drinking with "Xingyan" is only a little drunk, singing of "Xiaolin" with mountain streams and wind and moon. "Iron City" is quiet at night, with the sound of battle drums, and the lamp drags the drunken calligraphy column. Everything is a temporary lodging, and "Daosheng" magic is the way itself. Change the full blessing, "Shoulian" pearls are bright, "Yangchun" "Baixue" are difficult to harmonize. (Xu Xiaochu's harmony)

"Bai Xue" "Yangchun" music of great harmony, wonderful "Wen Qi" thoughts seize the work of heaven, crossing the "Jicheng" together to say goodbye to the "Moon," Shengpan Yasuong sings the ancient customs. Poet "Boyuan" sings white and harmonizes, may "Gongzhan" hear the lonely Tung tree. The child of the Ma family "Wuliang" lives in "Yiping," and peers are outstanding and enlightened "Shaochuan." The mighty river flows for thousands of miles, and the sand sinks. The "Iron City" opens the sleeplessness, who knows "Xiaochu." The first time I saw spring, "Guangfu" went upstairs, and early "Xingyan" frost curved around. The wine immortal fainted "Dachao" in the North Sea, and only "Xiaolin" hated the sea for being "small, Die." The dream wants to continue to startle, "XiaoJi" the rooster calls "Xingya" East "Folk, Yi" is originally on the same boat, sharing glory and disgrace, and no amount of "Daoban" can hurt the eyes. "Yu Shu" painting reveres the ancient country, and the gods of production compete to "seek the new." Many talents gather in Jiangnan poems, such as "Lanting Fangqi", four seasons of spring, and the age of "Yansong Zhi" is long, "Ji Yin Huan Huan" is the host and guest. (Zhou Bangjun's Harmony) (筹成）

Special Feature

Rihui Port

– Fang Pingfan

Rihui Port – a village not far from the city, yet completely different from it. Here, there are no tall Western-style houses, smooth asphalt roads, no enchanting jazz music, and no glittering neon lights. There are no girls at the forefront of fashion, no young masters living a bourgeois life... The so-called "port" has no huge warships or magnificent ocean liners, only tattered sampans strung together, floating from Jiangbei.

Here, you don't hear the calls of "Miss" or "Mister," or the kinds of sentiments like "I Love You" that assault your ears. Instead, you hear the cries of "Da Sanzi," "Gou Liuzi"... or "little bastard," "Damn you, you dare!" – all kinds of strange noises.

Aside from a few warehouses covered with sheet metal or tarpaulins on the banks, the rest are all thatched huts less than five feet tall. People live in these shanties like they are crawling, drawing water for washing and drinking from this muddy, yellowish river that contains an indescribable stench. "Hygiene" is, of course, out of the question!

The fragrance of cosmetics is even harder to smell! In hot weather, there's only the smell of laborers' sweat and the stench of rotting garbage baked by the sun.

An occasional chrome-colored Studebaker car passes by, the driver stepping on the gas pedal to go very fast, afraid that slowing down will cause the car to be tainted with filth. The ladies and gentlemen in the car press handkerchiefs tightly against their noses.

The nights are quiet, and the days aren't lively either. The strong men who live in these thatched huts go to pull rickshaws, the young ones carry baskets to work as garbage inspectors, and the women also have their own occupations – sewing skirts and catching lice.

In this lonely and desolate village, you can't go to Moganshan to escape the summer heat or see twin lotus blossoms at Qingyang Port. But sometimes, it gets a few artists who use this primitive type of slum as materials for paintings, putting it on the easel with light brushstrokes. But in their brushstrokes, there are golden thatched huts, a clear stream, small boats, and white geese – a whole picture full of poetic charm.

"Truly, the beautiful mind of a painter."

This is Rihui Port on the outskirts of the "Paris of the East!"
